O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine together with its filling, and I have finished it by its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is lost from everything else, so the sciences are perished and decayed, and there remains nothing but small descriptions in old books that have been moved by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and vanity, and the intentions are closed and the sciences are alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I will vivify it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of instruments for cauterization and other tools of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to climb in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of joints, and the arrangement and moving and resting parts, and from the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with work is little; and similarly in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that anyone who is not familiar with the things said before should beware lest they make an error and kill men; thus I have often seen many who meddle in this science abandon their knowledge and skill.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut into an abscess on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of her neck; wherefore so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it was not removed he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took in charge the leg of a duke from our land which was broken, and with the breakage had a wound; and the ignorant surgeon forced the break to be set on top of the wound with great haste, and did not leave any dressing on the wound, and left it thus until the end; and he commanded that it should not be undone, and remained thus so that the leg was completely inflamed and the foot came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him and I hastened to come to loosen the leg; and when I had loosened it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in any case the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who opened up an infected abscess and then inflamed it through the bad judgment of his skill.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when a chancre is pure of melancholic humor, it is not necessary to touch it with iron unless one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, most dear sons, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, one where there is danger in multiple dispositions; and I will show you each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Here is the translation:
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galens says in some of his warnings: "Do not concern yourself with any bad disease unless you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterizations and medicinal cauterizations, and it is the chapter ordered from head to feet; and about the forms of instruments, and tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and bandages and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and it is the chapter ordered with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from head to feet, and with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, so that we remember our work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the aid and harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest and most subtle science and secret answer; and many wise men have spoken about this, agreeing with it; and I was not sufficient for their words, because I feared the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally to all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments: namely, the hot temperament with material and the dry temperament with material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry temperament with material, some have divided and said that cauterization is great help; and others have said the opposite: that cauterization is of no use in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat or dryness; and he who said the opposite says that cauterization does great help in hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body of man and its moisture according to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true at times through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, don't intervene unless you are the one who has experimented and knows through long use the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of human temperaments, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the surprises and pace of time; we have no fear of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered and agreed to the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire-cautery is one of the secrets of cures, and more noble than burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the member that it burns, and does not harm another member if there is no name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines come from member to member by approaching, and bring diseases of grievous sanitation to the afflicted member; and it happens that the patient dies due to his highness and the goodness of his substance not doing so, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this in my experiments and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me to take away from you the secret which is answerable to fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out diseases from bodies, as philosophers say in demonstrating; accept it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done and selected patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the ensuing harm is put below by the aid of cauterization; and indeed, if the cauterizations are for necessary and pressing pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think it, dear son, as foolish physicians do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and they say so; but it is not so as they believe, because cauterizations are not just medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and surpasses medicine in its haste and virtue of its work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And a possible thing is that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and excesses are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless it is cauterization administered at the right time or place where there is little excess and moisture, as in cauterizations for dens pain and similar things, and this pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth anything after medicine, but their intention is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures in any disease and they are not effective, then we administer the cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with gold instruments is more gentle than with iron ones, and they did not say this except for the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the place where cauterization is done does not cause harm, but it's not true because I have tested it, and I found that it's true in some people; and gold cauterization surpasses iron one, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And besides, when you heat an instrument of gold, you don't know when it's heated by the color of the gold, and it soon cools down; and if you heat it too much, it melts in the fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use fire-cautery because we have made it appear suitable to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter from beginning to end, so that the way may be easier for you to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is worth against moisture and cold on the head, and there are two reasons for it: one because of a disease called "soda", and the other because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and because of a multitude of dreams, pains in the teeth and throat, and also for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, stroke, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the patient be purged by a solvent medicine, clarifying the head 3 times or 4 times, according to what the virtues and age and habit of the patient can tolerate; and then render the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit with his arms crossed between your hands, and put his hands on his lap; after that place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let your thumb be where it will come to, so it bleeds a little, and then heat the cauterization called "olivare", which is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make it descend and spread your hand little by little in rotating; then lift your hand suddenly, and reward the spot if you see bone 1 small grain; and if you don't see it, repeat the cauterization until you see the bone as I have told you; after take 1 handful of silk, and put a soft and fluffy cotton inside, and place on the spot, and let it be for 3 days; then apply a moist cloth in butter; and leave it on until the scab is removed; after cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacos" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when the wound stays open longer, it purges more; and therefore it helps more.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should burn the cauterization so long that part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others say that one should burn the cauterization so long above, and push it in as hard as possible to make a hole in the bone as wide as 1 vermicelli thread that women put in their hair for the humors to flow out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after one must heal and close it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be good in every way, except in some people where there is a sign of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave it alone; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we observe in other members; and also when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salve and gentle for me, and from this I work a cure, even if it seems to be assembled.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes to the entire head and lasts long, the patient should use year's balm and pills called "cochie", and purging of the head, oils, and plasters; and if one does the fire cautery that we have previously said, it is worthless.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of a strong nature, and it is not too cold; then one should cauterize below that fire cautery as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, make a fire cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery where it is called "vasselz"; and there is one place where you put poultices; and hold your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels too much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of this elsewhere; and it is necessary that the cauteries on the horns be more subtle than those with which one makes a hole in the middle of the head, and that's the form.
dou cautere dou chief	of the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and spreads to the eye, and the patient's head is purged by mundane medicines, and all the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases are done, and nothing helps: then one should do cauterizations according to two manners, that is to say of medicinal fire and of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicinal fire cauterization is that you take a piece of alum, remove the bark and mix it with one part to two parts of water, and then make an incision on the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can pour the alum mixture under the skin; and when it has been poured, bind and tighten well and leave it thus for 12 hours; then loosen it and wash away the alum mixture, and let the wound remain thus for two or three days; then put a poultice on top of butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment until they are healed; and if you see fit, make use of some burning medicines that I have written about or in the treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizing iron of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or clover with a small amount of curvature, and in the middle there appears to be a little opening; and one puts it on the painful place, holds one's hand and turns the fire slightly, until half of the spark of the coal is burned; and lift one's hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and discharge an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that, put cotton in the form of a seal, and put it on the place by three days; then put wet cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cauterizer called "cultellare", do so at all points, but be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not an old one.
de emigraine	of the migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the fire cauterizers previously mentioned for medicine and iron do not suffice, then it is necessary that you heat the cauterizer called "cultellare" until it is white; and then apply it to the painful place, a line of half a finger's length long, and lift your hand once, and strain so as not to cut the artery and not to go up to the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when eating, and the nerves have regard for it, lest spasm come to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and also for one who does not know what to do, and who is not experienced in this art; and leave the work in my way; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizers do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cauterizer that we have said in the chapter on extracting the artery, with the cauterizer that has two knives; and this cauterizer is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear due to coldness, and one has tried medicines that dissolve and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not subside, then heat this cauterizer called "poins" as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, prick the entire ear that is ailing, or around both ears if the pain holds in both, and move away slightly from the root of the ear after you have marked the place to burn; and have 10 pricks around each ear; then treat the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torment that must be cured by cauterization is not other than those that arise from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make a cauterization on those similar to those that come from scorched skin and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torment that arises from phlegm and idleness, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizers: one in the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and put the cauterizer in the part that appears healthy, and make the fire cauterization near the head of the ear above a small amount below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a piece; and leave the cauterizer until half of the spark is burned; and this is the form of the cauterizer:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the appearance of the cultellare that we have mentioned before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knives be a little larger; after, treat the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then make three cauterizers: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cauterizer on the mouth of the stomach; and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	Lying idle.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	To this disease it is fitting to give the patient large pills and pills of a gentle nature for the brain; afterwards, rinse the head of the patient thoroughly, and place on the occiput an ointment of mustard as written in the treatise on ointments; and that is the manner of cauterization: if you do it just as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is cured thus, good it is; and if not, then make three cauterizations on the head going down to the neck, with a space of two or three inches between each one; and cure him as you would others, and if you see any swelling, and the patient is suffering, then make one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and cure until he is healed; and it is called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of the chill of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is fitting that the head be cleared of years and what we have said before; afterwards, rinse the head of the patient, then make a cauterization on the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is fierce, then make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave it until the most of the burning is done, and lift your hand; afterwards, cure until he is healed, and it is called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization unless one is phlegmatic, and it is fitting first to clear the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from penitent medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, then make him gargle and massage the brain often with good meats; afterwards, rinse the head in the middle, and make one cauterization according to what we have said before, and one on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is fierce and suffering, then make cauterizations as I have said to someone who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and it is called "olivier" according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, then make one cauterization subtle in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the superfluities or moists are corrupted and thickened, then make those cauterizations of threads as we have said to someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink by which the brain may be cleared, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After rinsing the head of the patient; after make one turpentine of linen well made, like a circle, and put it in the head; and the patient should be crossed, and be well held from all sides; afterwards present the liniment, and moisten with butter of ancient herbs; and heat it over tempered fire, so that the skin can endure being poured on it; after empty the circle within the head, and let it cool down; and do this to the patient once a week for each one, with good governance, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize it by making several points all over the cauterizer.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cauterizing moistens the brain excessively; and then put on soaked cotton in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the swelling of the eyes.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When swelling comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink clearing the head, and ward off all moists, and make him sweat or bathe several times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After, command him to rest his head, and make a cauterization on the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the descent of swelling is together on both eyes, or if it is on one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the hair, and be the cauterization long according to the width of the temple; and take care not to let blood flow, and if you see too much blood issuing, then stop the bleeding as well as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at the incision how to stop it; and never make a cauterization or cut under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	Of the tears of the heart.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or under the arteries that appear on the forehead outside; and one sees that it is cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cauterization that I said at the beginning of the swelling descending to the eyes: one cauterization in the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations or incisions under the two bones; and if there is more need, then cauterize sagaciously above the scalp with each small cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Of the tears of the heart within the eyes.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three cooked nights' worth of drink; afterwards rinse his head, and make a cauterization on the middle of the olive cauterization; and make two cauterizations of the "clavilis" cauterization on the two scalps, one spot under the hair; and take care not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And that is the form of the cauterization which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this fire cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	because of which it is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you make two cauterizations on the two scalps as long as the scalp is; and do not leave your hand off until one-third of the parchment is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Of the hair which points at the oil.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never happens that the hair of the eyes is converted downward and points at the oil, and then one makes cauterizations according to two manners: that is to say, by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or cauterization by fire commands the patient to leave the hairs until they are long and equal; and if they point at their birth, then restrain his eyes so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then the patient places them in a healthy state; afterwards, sign on paper over the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and it begins with the sign below the hairs; then he puts damp cotton soaked in egg yolk and musk mallow on the eye, then heat the cautery whose form is...
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you signed bit by bit several times, so that the burns are laid out; and the sign of the health of the work is when you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted to the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and let it be thus three days, then put damp cotton in butter until the scabbing is removed; after that anoint with ointment until they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs come and the paper is softened then restart the cautery on that same place, just as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, so cauterize until the paper is lifted to its natural height, and be even, and do not prick the hair into the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment form like the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and live coal, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so it doesn't cool down, then apply it on the shape you made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it on paper over the eyes; and if the patient holds only in one eye, then you must work on that one, and if in both alike; and put damp cotton under the eye in egg yolk; and the patient's head should be in a healthy state and place your finger showing above the medicine, and press gently three times whenever the patient feels the burning of the medicine, because he feels the burning as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the morsication has passed, then lift up the leaf of water, and reward yourself if you see the parchment lifted as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is not so, then put medicine on the leaf or the medicine will have no work, until your works are equal and your eyes are in order; then put on a moistened cotton ball in butter as long as the ardent heat is gone, after the cure of the ointment which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to beware well of your work by great care that it does not fail with the help of others.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then restart the medicine on that place which has been made soft by the proper paper, just as you did before; after curing it until it is healed; and this is the form of the mint leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to these be your constructions; and do not respond with the right way to one who has study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	It seems like a new chapter or section starts here. The phrase "de la cure de fistule par cautere" suggests that the text is moving on to discuss a different medical procedure, specifically the treatment of a fistula (a abnormal connection between two organs or parts of an organ) using cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterized according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in your hand; and take hold of the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does he remove his head; after that put damp cotton soaked in egg yolk or persimmon juice on the eye; after that heat the cautery which is thus: and is shaped like the comb of a vulture, together with the cautery; if you see, so it is pointed from one head to the other, and if you see, so it is also like a tent; but notwithstanding, this one that is shaped is worth moving for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the purulence, and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and draw out what is inside the bowels; after that put hot cautery on it, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part of the nerve above the eye, so that your hands do not go mad; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization just to the bone, then it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then restart the cauterization once more, and another time if necessary, and let it be for three days; after which put a moistened cotton poultice in butter, and cure with drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, then put on corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered; and rule according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	You understand the fistula, and make an incision; afterwards, put in the slender camel's hair that is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it to the quantity of one third of a pound; and hold your hand with camphor firmly, and do not move the patient's head until the camphor melts and flows to his eye; and it is necessary that you put damp cotton soaked in egg yolks or awe on the patient's eye: the camphor so artfully opens the place of the fistula, and heals by marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cauterization we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer poultices to the navel, and bring the fistula back to its natural place in the navel according to what is proper for its own location.
des crevaices en levres	It seems like a new chapter or section starts here. The phrase "des crevaices en levres" suggests that the text is moving on to discuss a different medical procedure, specifically the treatment of cracks in the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times occur cracks in the lips that are called "pils", and even in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it in those cracks hastily until it comes to a point; after that treat the place with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	It seems like a new chapter or section starts here. The phrase "de l'aposteme de la goule" suggests that the text is moving on to discuss a different medical procedure, specifically the treatment of an abscess in the throat (goule).
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l'uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;
dou movement des dens	of tooth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but it doesn't work, then put the patient's head in your own; after warm up the cautery from which the shape will come later in this manner as if you were putting a cord around a tooth; and place hot hastenly inside the cautery and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and resume the cautery according to your desire; after fill the patient's mouth with salted water, and let it stay for an hour and then rinse.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture corrupted dried.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from coldness, whether it is hot or cold, and medicines do not work, then there is need of a cautery in two ways: the butter cautery and the fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is such that you take butter from a cow, and the end in a iron or earthen spoon; after take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and wet it with melted butter, and place it on the aching tooth quickly and hold until it cools down; and thus do many times until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton are soaked in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and then put one hot iron so that the fire comes to the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauterizing fire is such that you take a piece of iron or bronze, and it is thick enough so that the flames do not reach the mouth of the patient; afterwards, heat the cauterizer, from which the form will come forth, and place it on the wound and hold your hand until the cauterizer has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the application of this cautery, and then rinses the face.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of whatever head you want, and according to what you can do; and this is the shape of the cord:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of pus and cold moisture, and do not obey digestion through medicines, then use the cautery with hair on top, followed by the form that comes next; and have two openings for the fumes to issue from the cautery to the other part; and put the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery according to its size, and leave it thus three days; and cover with a moist cloth in butter until the boil is removed; after that cure the affected area with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moistures prevail on the channels of the body and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by soluble medicines; afterwards make a fire cauterization at the root of the throat, and take care not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn with hot coals but only a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards make another cauterization at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and be it the cauterization that is called "clavile" which we have the form before; and cure the place as we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of consumption
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every disease of the throat are of cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or heat, and the disease is old, then make two cauterizations on the thorax in the armpits; and another cautery between the breasts; and that is the cautery called "clavicle" according to the shape which was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cauterization in piercing all the points that are called "poins" of which we have the form before in the illness of the ears; and be the points up to thirty or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing the wound according to what is said above, and let the cautery be at three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore are the cauteries lighter, because you make three in one go.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After be careful with the patient on his back and sides; after lift the skin that is inside the titillate (or numbness) of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then warm up the cautery which has two nails like this shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the skin so that it is pierced up to the sides, and the figure of the cautery comes together with three cauterizations; and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery which has three nails, because the figure of cauterization are six cauterizations; and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and that is the shape of the cautery which has three nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is joined upon this one nerve, for which there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cautery perpendicular to the broken seal; after make the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cauterized nail, or many cauterizations in succession are pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is refilled, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come into the stomach to the point that it throws them out according to its complexion, and many cathartics are brought to him, and the usual ways of cures do not help him, then it is necessary for the patient to be put on his back, stretch out his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then he makes three cauterizations one below the other, under the rib cage, as much as a handbreadth, to all of the cauterized nail, and two cauterizations on each side up to the point where the figure of the cauterization is at three angles, with such space between one and the other that they will not be joined together when they move; and let the cauterizations be so deep that they penetrate the two parts of the key, and let the figure of the cauterizations be according to this form without deviation.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see it being cauterized with a great fire on the stomach according to this form; and whoever has fear of this cautery, cauterize in piercing and signifying above the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you see to be there; then cauterize the entire cautery that is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver is pained by cold and moisture and great windiness, so that it is greatly out of its natural complexion due to superfluities; and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, but it does not help them, then the patient must be covered with a heating cloth; and sign on the belly with three cauterizations according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, under the ribs, where the human's sides come together; and there should be a space of as much as an egg between each cautery; and the cauteries should be long like the body, and do not press too hard with your hand on all the cauteries; and it should burn only half of the skin, and the patient should stand upright on their feet; and if they cannot, then they should lie down, stretch out their legs, and raise their arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	Et if thy will is, then cauterize these cauteries with the cutlery, if thou art subtle and wise in the art, and beware that thou dost not burn all the key, for thou wouldst dry out all the body; and that it doth not come too near, for the keys are very subtle thereabouts, and thou knowest truly.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess on the liver, and thou wishest to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, the patient feels excessive pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure was done by the mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be seated on his head; and then sign above the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ray, because of which the form is.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the fire until the coals are burned out, and it comes just short of being extinguished, until the burning is all gone; after that, according to the cure of the sores as long as he is healed; and it does not behoove anyone to use this cautery except one who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly operate, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient ones said that one should make pleurisy cauterizations with aristologe roots, and in this manner: take a long root of aristologe, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and long as your arm; and wet it with oil, and put it on the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the thorax and the neck, and two small cauterizations a little below in the part that is under the beard; and two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining slightly to the rear; and one cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on either side of the breast outside the cautery which is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand at all, but rather make it openly like when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some old people say that someone should use a fire-like cautery similar to a razor, and heat it up and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess; and then the pain subsides, as we have said about the abscess of the liver.
