Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient now, or he dies instantly, or a fistula comes that cannot be cured.
de la mice	Of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse in accordance with what we have said about the divisions of cures, and it does not benefit, then there are three manners of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After I put the two bellows inflamed so that the heat is perceived from the other side, and then treat the fire cauterization, and thus there will be four; if you see, then cauterize completely the fire cauterization at three bellows.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has taken root through long time, and this is true as regards the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cauterization does not work on an edema, except by the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the kidneys, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the chest; and let the cauterizations be well close to the spot where the heat.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After that, let the cauterizer stay open to get a purplish color after a long time, and do not cease the cure of the patient after the cauterization; and healing will hasten, and both intentions will come together with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cauterizer for the belly is the key that we have shown before; and that one for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is put here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of yellowish dew, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the thumb and the finger; and lift your hand with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go in too deep, lest the yellowish dew becomes fierce; and let the cauter be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauterizations on each leg at the point of the cuticle; and let the cauterizers be long, one under the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauterizers open for a long time without healing, until the pus comes out; after that, cure with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When a discharge from the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by manners of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having strong vigor, then make one great cauterization on the stomach according to what has been spoken here before about the stomach cauterizer, at the circulatory cauterizer; and three subtle cauterizations around the belly, each one a small key, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cauterization on the wrist, and one cauterization on each elbow, and two small cauterizations on the stomach near the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and made up of cold, moist, corrupt humors, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely under the almond tree and very small and triangular in shape; and one cauterization below the mouth, two on the shoulders; and if you think his stomach has been chilled, and the food does not cook, and one sees his face inflating, then make a great cauterization on the stomach, as is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the intestines at every cauterization point; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure, let the joint be so long as it is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the choleritis which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the choleritis, heat the cauterizer which seems like a razor, and then put it entirely ablaze on that choleritic cut; and let your hand be there until the cauterizers come to the birth of the vein, so that the blood will not flow; make this once or twice, and if there is much choleritis, then cauterize each one as we have said; after that, cure with ointments that are profitable until they are healed; and if you cauterize a great cauterizer on the navel, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes, and it is inflamed and discharges corrupted putridity and moisture, then you must carefully examine the entire tent and know how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After you have cauterized the area that seems to be the rawest, and plug it into the fistula according to the size that the tent has entered, and re-cauterize until the corrupted flesh is burned away, once, twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of harm; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder and into the intestine, then beware of these parts, and do not burn any further unless it is in a well-warmed place, and think that it is not perished; after the cure, let the joint be so long as it is sound, and if the part is swollen, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the part is entirely healed; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the part is troubled, and corrupts the bone at its root; and thus as one of those things we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	From the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys and great windiness, and does not take on a womanly form, then it is necessary that you make a fire cautery on the kidneys from one side and another at the cauterized clave that we have mentioned before; and if we were to cauterize in mid-air, there would be three cauterizations in a line, and they will do more great aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a fire cautery on the part outside of the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and one to the right and one to the left, each being as long as the length of a foot; and make one cauterization behind the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be clave-shaped according to the form mentioned earlier.
de la marris	Of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for this reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms are late; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that one make three cauterizations around the belly, as we have said in the fire cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be clave-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the groin of the hainche, and because of this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints of the departure are found, then you must cauterize the patient on the groin of the hainche with one cauterization resembling a circle, and sign before the joint around the groin as it turns, so that the groin be inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which one has cauterized in the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three great cauterizations of the olivaire, and let them be as deep as all the layers; and cure it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin of the hainche, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two ways: that is to say with hot medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, one of which is: that you cauterize on the ridge of the backbone three triangular cauterizations according to this form, and make good depth and great, and have between each cauterization the width of a thumb, and be the cauterizations oval; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the top of the backbone, why there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the cauterized circle that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hainche; but make it in this manner so that the circles contain all the hainche, and all the fibers of the layer are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the back and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, one makes two cauterizations on each side where the patient says the pain holds, and one cauterization above the ankle four thumb-widths from the part on the left; and be the cauterizations cutaneous, and be the thickness of a key ashed; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two toes or nearly so, one makes three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then make more; and if it is known that the pain is below the kneecap towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the cutellaire or circular cauterization, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave out so much of the cauterization as to burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more great annoyance and contraction for the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they were left until the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and were pierced and corrupted all over the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purgation of belly which brought about his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say in the cauterization of the groin, this is why it is done, make such an iron and let it be at the head as thick as a walnut from date, or a little less, and let it be between the thumb and finger, and so that one is between the fingers just about the length of a pea; and the spaces should be two parts, and they should also be like beans, and there should be one iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is entirely red and gives off an odor, then put it on the swelling of the wounded thigh, and be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once .i. cautery again and leave for three days; and then grease with butter, and let the wound remain open a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery because of the fear of his regard, and if we see one who uses it; and nevertheless these are good cauteries which can be endured by those where it affects.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you make the instrument to join together in which the edges of the gate descend, and it is made of earth or iron with one appearance long, and in the height have two noses, and have between each the quantity of the thickness of a doves; and they be open above and below, and come together in this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place the boil of the armpit on the patient lying on their side, and afterwards put your hand above the boil of the armpit; then pour between the two circles of hot water which has been heated over a fire to boiling point, and let it leave one hour of time, and allow the patient to suffer the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds a similar biting as of fire; and when the biting is passed, take your hand with the instrument and lift the boil of sweet water, and leave it thus for three days, and put on butter until that which is black from the scab is removed; and then let it be for three days that the purtification may cease; and this would be the final aid after the cure of ointments as long as they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the hip or leg, make an instrument that holds it thus as you have done in the natural manner; and this is the method of hot water, and I have written it or treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot water, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	or there is a small hole to drain what the point of a razor can enter; and put it on top of one pot into another well-plumbed pot, and put sweet water above, so much that two layers of powder are above you will have it well prepared in your hand; and leave it thus until the water drains and becomes clear or murky in the bottom pot, then take all that water and pour it onto hot water and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	Et lors si sera much anguish and is administered in movements of medical works and in cauteries of other members. For it does a good work like fires, and if to other medicines that one cauterizes well the flesh thus as theriac and honeyed myrrh and chalcedony with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure where one man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and he highly praised it, saying that no other cure was done, and that he was healed at once when this cure was performed, and he bathed himself just as is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this same way that you take fresh and dry litargy, and pound it much with a little bit of grease, and put it on the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it there for three hours, or until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath until his body is somewhat warmed up, and then make him get into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery on such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair, it helps a lot; and one should make the cauteries in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called the interdigital space.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that take goat's hair that is dry, and set it on fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the linen, and leave it until it is extinguished; and do this again, and do not stop doing this until you think by sense that it will reach as far as the groin, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat's hair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or from too great evacuation, or from similar signs of expanded cold matter, none of these likenesses is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be rid of fetid pills or other similar things, which one makes on the back, there where the pain stays, three lines marked with enche, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and make the cauteries according to the "poins" cautery; and if you see fit, do .iii. cauterizations or .iiii. at the middle hinge of the cautery clamp in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have stiff backs when they rise, and fear; and you find in the lower back and in no other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and it is being cured, then cauterize it with the "celcle" cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery equates each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with the fire cautery at two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, let the limb be so until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cauterization in a place where there may be swelling of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which physicians properly call "podagre", and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make the cauterization to all the cauterization which one calls "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make a cauterization on each knee three or four times, for all the olfactory cautery; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand away from that place until the fat of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then make pungent points around the wrist two lines; and if there remains no pain to the shoulder, then make pungent points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the armpits or just to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do good governance and purge phlegm, then it will be cured through the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the ligament
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itch comes in the angles, and the boils descend to the groin and it is newly, then it is necessary that when you see it being cured, he does not move at all that day; and that he uses things which loosen the bowels, so that the wind descends from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath as long as the boils are repaired, and then cauterize at the enche below the itch on the bone of the shoulder, and make a sign like the middle of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with the form that is as follows:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and lets out stools.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and the attendants hold his hand so that they do not return back; and work well on the patient's hips, and put a cushion and a servant under him on the hips, and another under his breast who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of all your hand, and keep it straight and keep it until you reach the bone, and if you do not hit it the first time, so repeat it again as many times as necessary until you reach the bone; and be careful subtly that the bowels do not escape when you are doing the cautery; lest you burn him; and lest through this the patient die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone at the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their size, and those of big people also as big according to theirs; after three days, clean the place where the cautery was done with butter until the scabbing is removed; afterwards, treat other wounds until they are healed, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that their bandages be left long enough, so that the flesh does not burst when he will want to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, give him a well-made bandage and have it on for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not exert himself too much and watch out for excessive drinking of liquids and eating, and loud shouting; and when he follows this instruction, he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say later on in this chapter, cut to shape.
de la routure dou ventre	of the itch of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow more, then make the fire cautery of the same quantity, and let the third part of the incision be burnt; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the old men say that one should cauterize the ulcer at three angles in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the beginning of the incision and make a line along the length above the ulcer, and another below, and lead your hand all around the entire cauterization.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more fragile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cauterization called "poins", and let the cauterizations be according to the length of the member, its smallness and weakness, and its virtue and location in terms of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, it's well; if not, start another one on that spot, for such cases are when the patient should be changed to the member that is nearby, so you should do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The members are helped sometimes by a cautery with great assistance, and similarly the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you not see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not leave or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may pervade all of the patient, then make four cauterizations on the head: one through the forehead to the nose, and another from the forehead to the eyebrows; and two on each horn, and one behind on the hairline; and leave your hand there until the cauterization reaches the bone, and until the crusts come out so that the vapors of gross humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the mole according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is spread everywhere and it is manifestly dying, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head, one in front of the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and six on the spine of the back, and one large on the croup and one other below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the flanks, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and take care of the nerves that are behind the last vertebra, so you don't burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, more I do of cauterizing,
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizing be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward, wash the wound with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, and it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the member according to its greatness and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little bit within the skin of the flesh; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one does cauterization on the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but however, no one should meddle if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine does not bring any benefit, then one cauterizes with a cautery a little bit deep, according to the quantity of the hollow of the knee, until the discharge is removed, and its color is changed; then cure with farina mixed with dates and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and with blood from colander and almond, each one in equal parts; and mix everything together, and tie it up in a cloth, and apply to the wound as long as he is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancres by fire
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with the fire cautery that appears like a circle, all around the tour of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem to me good, for I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen some time; and more rightful thing is that it be cauterized around, with the fire cautery that is called "circule", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it delays in dying or because of the superfluity it makes or because of the old age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the weather; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries that prick; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through the skin, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in this manner as if the course of the purging were eased.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a consumption of member, for it consumes members just as fire consumes dry flaxen.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can suffer both fire and cautery together, then sharpen the cauterizers to be very small and great, according as it is fitting for the part or the disease; after which cauterize all around until you have removed all the corruption, and nothing remains but what is corrupted is taken away.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized wounds softened with oil until the scorchings of fire are removed, and all corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments brings forth a scar.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that a healthy scar does not form, it is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery to what remains of the corrupted wounds.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy is sometimes cured with medicinal aloe instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for medicinal aloe in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The hairs which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Very often happens that on the feet due to something outside comes a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a big ugly thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cauterization of this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is known that it is fire cauterization and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is when you heat the cautery iron as hot as a vulture's pen, and make it of good iron to the measure that it can pierce through all parts, and have subtle edges; after that, put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the end of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then make a poultice with wild marjoram crushed with oil, and let the poultice be on all night, and the nail will fall off and be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound by pouring in oil as long as it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Et si ils sont convertis par défauts loin du corps, et maintes fois adviennent en mains et à pieds, si convient que tu y amenistres cautère d'eau chaude; et est en tel manière: pren une cagne d'argile ou de fer, ou une pene de vouteul, et met sus le clou et l'autel, c'est à savoir porrets vertus; et met la caine sus si qu'elle pourprigne tout entour, puis i met un poc d'eau chaude, et retiens bien ta main, et presse ta main en tournant si que les marge de la caine viennent à la racine du clou, et puisse trouver l'eau chaude voie parfonde jusque'à la racine; et souffre le malade un poc la mordication de l'eau chaude une heure; puis le laisse ensi, et il se déracinera tous à tout ses racines.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So treat another after, as long as you have reached all those within the body, then heal the wounds that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cures of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble because of cold or numbness, or quartan fever or other causes, then it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the belly, and one on the olive-shaped area of the stomach; then let the trembling cease, and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes apparent on the surface of the cleansed body, or foul ulcers, which come from great corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at first when they appear, one should make a fire cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that the point be taken up by the fire, or of long aristolochic root, or a lentiform cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes when one cauterizes at the beginning as this manner appears, and they cannot grow further forward, but are broken off the superfluous parts that come from them, and are healed; but it is necessary for this to be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times it happens that great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes from external causes, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you hasten to place your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tightly until the blood is calmed under your fingers, and no more flows; then take up to the fire small and large olive-shaped cauterizers, all red ones, as many as there are; then take one, great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place it on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery so long until the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts bleeding again when you lift your fingers off the vein, and the cautery has cooled, then take quickly one other of the cauterizers that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the blood is staunched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is below, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well staunch it oneself, especially if the artery is large, unless it be by one of the three manners we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to staunch blood; and let it be tied and strained correctly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring about staunching by binding tightly with cloth or putting hot things on it, or similar things, if there is no benefit unless a little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch well until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water frequently so that it is very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and staunched; and make inquiries ahead about those things which he needs for cauterizers and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases in which it is necessary to make a fire cautery or apply hot medicine, and the wounds, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go through this chapter by the same way so that one may find more easily what one wishes.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore that I begin this, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and for this reason it is necessary to take greater care.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to take a foolish risk.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many people come seeking cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have been so harmed by their disease that they will die quickly due to the harshness of their disease and the greatness of its malice; and one should fear such cases.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these are those who give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you yield to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of and can gain and lose; and use pronouncement and indication in the cures of your sick to convert salvation; and this will help you achieve good reputation, and glory, and praise-worthy memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement and droiture, and se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauterizations, which I have described from the beginning to the end, so that you may find more easily those things of which you will have need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of water from the head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this sickness often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife holds too tightly the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown to us.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this sickness other than in children, and all those that I have seen died; and therefore it seems to me that it is not worth bothering with such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew bigger each day until it could no longer be borne; and believed so much moisture that he would die, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone above the skull, between the skin and the bone; and the treatment is such when the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you cut into the head a gap wide; and it should also be as long as two nuns, until the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the head opened on each side, and the water jumps forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and this does not come to you: then it is necessary that you cut into the head three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract all moisture entirely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After having bound the cuts with cloths and powders, and applying wine and oil, and leaving it so for five days; then he loosens it, and treats the wound with tents and ointments, and lets the head swell equally, and then allows the patient to eat dry food without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens up and the moisture gathers; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens up and the moisture gathers, and make an incision according to what you are able; and be careful not to cut the artery; and note that there is a flow of blood, so that the patient may die from the bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or at the pit, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is the cauterization with what will be applied to the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you are about to cover the views, the patient must bend their head back; afterwards, they scrub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient removes their neck from the cloth; then look where the vein bleeds, and the pulse of one and the other is felt after the ears, and it is responded; then mark the pulses in an arch, then cut both with a sharp spatula for two parts, so that the wound comes to the bone, and this should be by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as two do across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will jump out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to sensing, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign by the incision and make just up to the bone; and what is needed for blood to be put outside is six c/ and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point out the siphac, so that apostemes do not come forth there, then strain the wound and tie, and the cure with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and sharp headache, because of the moistures of tears and heats in temples and old forgotten things and similar cases, and it is treated by methods of medical cures and all that does not help, we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have counted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient bends back his temples' hairs, and feels for the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little responded except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responded, then extract the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and soak the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which there is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it above the pincers, and depart well from the threads that are below each part; and if the artery is subtle, then turn it to the point of the unciné, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	If she isn't cut, then the blood won't flow at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain the blood of .vi. c., down to .iii.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double strong silk thread, so that no bleeding occurs before the wound is sealed, and there will be a flow of blood; then cut off the superfluity that is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the area with the cutlery knife down to the bone until the arteries are cut; and this is the main work, if the patient does not have a fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is help to finish the moisture: that's why it is of greater aid to moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the wound with old cotton and puts on well-made tents; and when one removes them, be careful to apply medicines that make flesh grow and tents, until they are healed; and if without any doubt from the artery as long as you work there, hasten to cauterize by fire or employ the leaf of vitriol and strain it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don't have what's present, put a cloth on the wound so that the blood congeals, and raise the wound with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as necessary. And what is most important and lighter in the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting into two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to ward off heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a space of about an inch, and then when you have signed for cutting into the two joints, and you must use the hot iron on one side as far as the bone, and cut the vein in both joints; and let them be separated between the two shoulders because it is not connected with this cautery from top to bottom; and that's the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
