Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the head of the knee, and grows and becomes great after a while, until it is seen as something to behold; and because of this, you must cut it off at the beginning, and remove all that remains, then put on the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it off until it is great, then take heed if it is hard, with a flux of color, and poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touchment, not of flux of color, and you see that one can remove all of it, then empty the patient and remove the cutting without fear, and cure the knee with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the knee is cut off and bound
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuity come in one of these cartilaginous works, it does little good, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to do thus with whoever has it, if one looks and sees that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together at a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from one part and another, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their keratin until they heal, then bring the two lips together at a seam, and bind it, and powder on top with blood of dragon, and frankincense; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster of force or other plaster suitable, and leave it as long as it cleans itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the seam is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have abscesses inside their lips that are hard, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut each one open, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply the lip after the incision with vinegar powder, until the blood is stopped; and then anoint with oil, and cure the lip with dry things as much as it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a joined flesh grows on the gums that the ancients call "albulus"; then it is necessary that you support it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the bow or blood flow; then put vinegar powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it off again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and this is the form of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the ears
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, raw and rough excrescences that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; then it is necessary that you sit the patient in your hands, and make his eyes be in your sight, and remove the teeth or excrescences as they appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and verdure, and yellowing and other discolorations, until they are purged; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it's good; but if not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scraper used to remove teeth has other forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth with its pain, you should delay pulling it as long as you can, for it must not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, almost to the point where one has no excuse to regret.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to pull out, then you must be certain of the tooth that is aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient's pain is many times caused by a toothache, and he thinks it is the tooth of Saint Denis, and makes him pull out the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart at all from him until the bad humors are removed, for we have already tried this with these saints. And when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then you must scrape around the tooth in every direction, making it strong to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your two hands or fine pincers at the first pace and pace, until it is well extracted, then secure the pincers; and let the patient's head be in your holy hand between your knees, and hold him steady so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each part, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Et if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it should be filled with drapels there where the perforations are; and if it is strained gently with pincers, so that it does not break when being strained; and it is necessary to work carefully around the gum for dislodging the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and have the patient return with greater pains in the tooth caused by the root's wickedness than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like foolish surgeons who, through their haste and boldness, break the cartilage sometimes, and do not bring about what we have recounted; but they often cause great harm through the roots that remain, or by breaking the cartilage, as we have seen many times; and when the tooth is loose, wash it with wine, or vinegar, or seaweed; and if bleeding occurs there, as it often does, fill the wound with vitriol paste; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, to which one must first bend the teeth, are long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth to hold the forceps.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the exit, it is necessary that you put a dampened cotton or cloth on the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the flesh is softened, then put in forceps called "algefri", by which the head appears to be shaped like a scythe; and make them also as a file is formed.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire gum around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a paline, by which there is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, by which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two jaws, by which there is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great forceps, by which there is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should be so strong that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments that are not counted; and wise master surgeons find for themselves their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease shows them, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases; and if one breaks the carriage or some other bones, or it is possible, then one seeks out instruments as I have said, and helps with gestures, by which there is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove; and then restore the wound with medicines suitable for this case, and if there is in the bone a putridity, and it is small, then resect all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape in the body, and the form is ugly, and especially in maiden women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly formed after the previous one, and is not in its right place, and cannot be straightened or filed: then cut; and if it is adjacent to the tooth, take this instrument which has the shape, and is similar to a small beak, and be made of well-forged iron with an edge.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file files slowly piece by piece in a few days due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; and if it appears that one can file it, then use a similar file as this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth slowly piece by piece over a few days, so that it does not move until it takes shape; then smooth it out at the end to any scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and bleeds the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose in front, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press down on what they eat without spitting it out, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, but it does not work; then it is necessary to restrain them with a golden thread, for silver threads become green and rot, but gold never changes; and let the middle thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth directed, take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the head between my teeth, if there is one or more, until you come to a bleeding just up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again just to where you started, and restrain your hand subtly and gradually, until it does not move anymore; and be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the threads of the silk to a pair of pincers, and assemble them, and re-point between two healthy teeth, so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then let it be thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it comes loose, or the strings break, then tighten with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of two healthy teeth, and two molars, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	When the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place gradually, piece by piece, as we have said; and do not intervene unless you are a wise and patient person, and sometimes make the shape of a whalebone tooth, and put it back where the defect is, and hold it so as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this bond which comes under the tongue or naturally, except when one is born thus; or by accident of a sewn wound; and the work is such that you will work on the patient's mouth, and have their head in your healthy state, and lift up their tongue; then tie off the nervous thread from the wide one, so that the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it's due to a sudden wound, then soak the bandage and tie off the wide one; and be careful not to make the incision too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, lift up the red rose water and soap, or cold water, then put a linen tent under the tongue; and let the patient wear it each night, so that the wound does not harden.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if haemorrhaging occurs, then place on the glassy surface of the vitriol, and if the bleeding is great, then cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is green or black or hard, so the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor and there is moisture, then pour on the unguent, and make a subtle poultice with spathium, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the blood flows at your operation, put vitriol powder on top until it is stanchied, then return to your operation as long as you are finishing up; then lift the ease and silk water, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No boil comes within the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "II amandres"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and fusel color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch with iron, also for the evacuation of blood; but leave it until it is dry, and then you will cut it, or it would break apart on its own; and if it is of whitish color and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess has ceased to pulsate and is quieted.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Make the patient sit before the sun, and his hands be in good condition, and work the mouth and grasp the servant's fingers between his hands, and press the tongue downwards to all the instrument, which is the shape; and it should be of silver or subtle iron just like knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And can you press the tongue onto all this instrument and see the abscess, then take the unguent and insert it into the almond-shaped swelling, and draw it upwards as far as you can; and do not touch anything with cloths, then cover it with the instrument, so that it takes its shape, which seems like a force; and yet the head is curved, one side to the other, and are very hard, and is made of iron or lead.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cover it with forceps, so that it takes its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be torn from one side and the other; and when you have covered one of the almonds, then cover the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and with warm water and ease, and if bleeding comes, gargle the patient with hot water, or grated apple skins that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanchied; then cure it as long as it is healed; and sometimes abscesses arise in the throat other than the two almonds, so cover them then in the same way as the two almonds similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I healed a woman from an abscess that was situated inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense; and I had well closed off all the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had pushed out two streams through the two holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and inserted an instrument into one nostril, then I drew forth pus, and with it a great deal of blood; then I refilled the other nostril, and had the patient's mouth open and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the instrument into that abscess, and cut out a part, and only a little bit of blood flowed out; and thus the conduit of the throat was unclogged in the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recurred again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; afterwards I bound it up and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and only God did anything with them after me.
de l’uve	of the olive oil
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the veins descend to the eye and are swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if they are below a large rounded one, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the swelling of the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to cut it; and if it is rounded and not long; and it is sanguine or of a reddish color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to make the patient sit before the sun and press the tongue against the instrument which we have remembered here before; then insert the lancet into the vein, and draw it down, and cut with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the superfluity that is beyond natural limits; for if you cover more, it causes harm to voice and speech; and after incision, use what we have said in the incision of two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about covering, you should use cunning at the cauterization to eliminate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument we have said in the chapter of cautery, and mixes with sharp, living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and by using the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a head or hair that one applies the medicine to, just as the hives of a beekeeper, and places the instrument on all the medicine above the ulcer; and the patient should lie on their side with their chest open, so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and lungs. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the ulcer for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it is numb and the effects of the medicine are calmed; and if you need, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in a tube above, until the cotton covers the ulcer; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to begin the medicine cautery again, then begin it again, and after the cautery, surround the ulcer with cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse everything around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and cared for gargling until one is well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not to mention the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them into one pot, and add oil, and let it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with firm earth, and inside the pot have one instrument made in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is of silver or lead, and whether one of the keys is thrust into the patient's mouth so long as the vapor rises to the eye through the vein, so long as the eye is deadened; after which it often recommences, so long as the eye dries, and be sure you do not do this at the beginning of the hot aposteme, for many things happen there; nor do this only when the hot aposteme declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cord and put a piece of egg-white inside the head, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the egg-white does not allow the vapor to weigh heavily on the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens that there is a lump at the throat or spine of fish or something; so it is necessary to treat what you can see and press the tongue on the sun over all the instrument until you see the thing move; and what does not open up and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing escapes through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or one quarter of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, then pass it through; and when it comes to the light, it will harden, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the top so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the top raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, lest all go wrong, nor push the bone inside; and move slowly so that the patient puts the instrument in, for it is necessary or the thing to be forced out; then put it down, or pull it out along the entire instrument evenly, until it is completely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for the sanguineous humor, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not profit, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see pus, then remove it bit by bit with a small incision or with subtle forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a hairy cord, and tie it around the patient's neck, then heat the knot of the cord by fire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is troubled with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full pitcher of cold water, and pour it into the mouth, and let it flow without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the pus feels the water, it will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not vomit as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asafetida at the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will purge without hesitation.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has hot coals, and let the cloth be covered with a perforated cover in the middle, and in that hole put the key of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cainne in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes just to the sweat; and the sweat falls now, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to come forth by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to remove the mucus is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved forceps for moving into the throat; and has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and has lime-like roughness, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and look at this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what remembrance comes afterwards in this book from one and the other, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners in which the one is like itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those with wounds on their body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not puncture until the bowels have matured according to their completion; and if there are such that it is necessary to puncture when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, just as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is surrounded by pus, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes a contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main member; or it is near the foundation, if one pierces it when it is rotten; and it is not necessary that you puncture a ripe abscess without digestion being complete, except for that which is near the foundation, so it does not spread deep, become elongated inside, and turn into a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Et covient que tu saiches l'oure de la perforation de l'aposteme qui est meur selonc l'acomplissement, and that is when the pain is assuaged, and the departements of fever, and the diminishment of pain and heat, and of debate and of setting right the head of the aposteme, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation sit in relation to the aposteme, or more dependent on its place, and where it appears to move; and the perforation be long in the body, and if the apostemes are at hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal or where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who suffer, by reason of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh hardened, so it is necessary that you leave the puncture alone until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture before that, it will be stretched out the body from the vein of him, and it is full of much foul matter; and by chance harden the lips and inner parts of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the members need it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small holes; and large incisions for large abscesses, and many cuts according to the likeness of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become as dry as a cloth, and is exhausted, then do as one does with babies: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those whose edge is cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of angels; and if there are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil who have not a chief, such as aposteme soffre superficial, it is necessary that you pierce thoroughly; and it is necessary when the apostemes are great, and it has gathered a great bow, and you pierce, if you do not pull out all the bow in that hour, but one part; then stop the aposteme just to the other day, then pull out nothing from there again; do this by many times, gradually, until the bow is entirely gone; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or elderly men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits jump out at times with the issue of the bow, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then therefore use this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your aposteme, if the wound bleeds, and look if the wound of the aposteme is small; and if it's a plain cutting, then try to place a tent made of linen or old cotton; and if it's large apostemes, and there are many cavities, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come together; and if you have cut into the aposteme part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or a rag of linen without moisture, and tie it just to the third day; then remove it, and cure it with oil until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if hemorrhages of blood occur at your operation, then apply cold and easy water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hemorrhages of blood persist, then apply governance and care, and the powders that I have said to put in wounds in this book, and if it's in the time of winter, and the wound or abscess is very nervous, then you must put on wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it's in summer, and the wound is fleshy, then you must put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and scab and treat, as is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this should be known universally in the treatments of apostemes: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatments of apostemes, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and there are ways of ours that are like those in fabric, just as a tailor has with a silkworm, and many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some big and such ones where there is moisture like pustules; and if there are some that are hard and stony to the knife, and one has no doubt if the artery does not make it contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of tailoring are that you must test all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes hereafter, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then let it dry on top of a long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape off without leaving anything on the skin that contains that moisture, for it will return again if you leave anything; then plunge cotton into Egyptian oil, if it is present; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply the dressing to the wound, and let it be until the next day; and those who are left of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton, just as before, on the second day and third day, until you know well that it does not linger at night; then treat the wound with ointment as needed, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, so cut it according to this form, from long; and remove all your poultices, and scrape off all around, and put all your care in drawing forth what lies beneath the cloth where it is situated; and if the artery does not agree with you, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly do with the abscess if it is pitted, and cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the pitted abscess and the moist one, if it is more lightweight, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in some of these abscesses or the head, nor any moistness in those abscesses that I copied from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess just like a whitened stone, rough and pale, and it could not be broken; and if one had been made of it, it would have caused a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of ears, the opening should always be as dependent on the place as possible so that the pus may issue forth; and the cure should be done as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck and below the armpits, and sometimes in the groin, and occasionally elsewhere on the body, and they swell, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	Each scrophula is properly within its own coat, just as the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said; and similar things to these scrophulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Then, since you see a good condition for cutting, and it resembles the color of the flesh, and is quiet from all sides, and is not near the nerves of the neck or artery or conduit, and is not very deep; so it is necessary that you cut above, and scrape each part, and take the two lips of the key as one, if you need to, just as we have said in abscesses of the head; and proceed gradually, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor should it be the spatula-like nor trenching, lest your hand escapes, and you do not see too far ahead, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that stop bleeding, and bind the wound; and leave it so that the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it; and then examine carefully if there are any small scrofulae remaining, cut them and scrape them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it's not necessary to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then apply the wound with old Egyptian cotton dipped in egg yolk, then heal.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you drain the entire scrophula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, then there will be no remaining superfluity because of the greatness of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw forth the pus, and sew if as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophulas that hold superfluity, pierce there where it appears to be most swollen; and the piercing is done as with the one mentioned before, depending on this, then tents are applied with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of the corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleaned, then the ointment treatment is discontinued, until it is healed.
de squinance	of swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones used to say and talk about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have swelling, it is necessary that the cut in the throat which is called "epiglote" be avoided; and this is not done by them, because all the veins and the pores of the patient are hot in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both sides.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to escape the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four a small incision through the thickness, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syphac, not in the cartilage; and those things are suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the surrounding area, then cuts the leather so far as it comes to the chin; and avoids the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then takes out the sponge, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein at the chin which jumps forth through the torn place and due to the loss of voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed about which one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound of the skin, and sew it all together without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this just yet, until the throat is entirely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the fault is going astray.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then take out the epiglote for this reason, because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded against death; and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden take a knife, and she stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the womb; and I was called to cure her, and found her thus as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and saw well that she had not cut any vein or guided it far beyond the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was healed; and it happened to the maiden that she regained her voice, and afterwards returned to her usual state; therefore I say that in cutting into the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it occurs mostly in women; and it occurs according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or natural ones have no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is according to two manners, as one that resembles fat in us, and another manner that resembles an abscess that comes from an artery; and it has fear, and should not be treated as if it were a great abscess, but rather one that is small, and prove and search all around: if you find it like this, without fat and unable to move at all, then cut it off, just as we cut into fat, and treat it thoroughly until there is no more; and search well everywhere, and cure it as needed, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of noses
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways we are, of which I will say all similarities; and now it is necessary that I tell all the difference that is between our joint and its exit.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the exit is hot and feverish, until the ebullition has passed, and the purulence is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the joint there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains its own sac, which is its own pouch and is in accordance with the color of the body, and begins just like a seed, and becomes large; and it is according to two appearances, either fatty or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the nose, that you examine and inquire first by all the instruments which are called "intimate", according to what its form comes or according to the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of incision for abscesses is that you take the most moist part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two paces back and forth, until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the foreign object, and be careful so that it does not spring forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j'ai dit des autres apostemes;
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it remains nothing, then the wound comes back many times; and if there is some left and the blood grieves, then apply the wound with certain corrosive powders, and bind the wound, and put on soothing things that are hot, and cure with other cures until it is healed; and if the wound is large, then cut off both lips of the wound, and cure what remains.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein swells up and is contrary to you or another obstacle hinders you, and you are in a hurry, then apply the broken vitriol, and let it remain for two or three days until the wound heals, and stop the bleeding of the blood; then return to the needlework that remains from the thread.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the shapes of the instruments entangled, and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb"; and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, in order to encircle the apostemes of fistula; and they are also like needles with which one sews sorceries, and are made of yellow citrine, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most valuable; and they are more proven for black pitch to encircle the corbeurs of fistula; and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	Forms of tumors are many and similar, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and some tumors have two crevices of three kinds also; and some with three crevices, and they are the same in three ways; and some with two crevices, and one tumor with only one crevice, and they are the same in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharpened, and some have only one edge from which you scrape the flesh, so that you do not cut the vein or nerve; and among these introducers are those wrapped in cloth, so that the patient does not feel anything at the opening of abscesses; and they come in three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one only uses them on a charmed place, such as joints, arms, breasts, and ribs, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another little instrument, resembling the edges of files, according to this form, at which blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put sometimes in a place where the wound heals by closing the veins and arteries, and sometimes again according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Breasts swell in some men when they begin to corrupt, until they seem like women's breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to treat according to this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine allowing the flesh to form a scab, then bring together the two lips of the wound at the seam, and care for it until it is healed; and if the breast dips downward, and is swollen due to its greatness as in women, so cut it in two folds above, by two similar splits; thereby one will hold to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.; then scrape off the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about seams and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully done, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the discharge of blood, so it is necessary that you fill the wound with damp cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it has consumed the remaining flesh and fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	I assume this is the title of the section or chapter in the text, which translates to "About Abscesses of Armpits".
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas or those with edges, and among them are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture need to be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
