And if the wound is great like a cut with a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and gaping, and barely holds together by a thread, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, just like poults, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	Et if you find the porriture on the hide and it's not on the bone, then cut out all the porriture and throw away the bad part, and then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without delay, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then take the artery and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put in this powder which solidifies even when air has changed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live coal, and mix the powder subtly, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then tie it well, and let it be without loosening, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is fully healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one never does this with coal alone, unless one has neither incense nor blood of dragon, but only when the air has changed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil has moved the wound, even to its place, then do not put on this powder; but put on some digested ointments or flour of barley made with water and honey, until it drips downwards; then cure him with other cures until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone break comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there being no difference between it and one of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the cure and not put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be soft, as one would wash in sweet water, and mix it with rose oil, and wash it also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up with threads, then apply a dressing until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	Et si les plaies sont parfondes et élevée et pleine de boue, alors la perce ou plus bas lieu; et si l'artère est coupée, et décomposent le sang qui en vient, alors la désouvre, la lie, et la cautériser se met en œuvre; et si l'épine de la gorge est coupée, ou les coueurs, et le conduit est gardé, par quoi la viande va, alors coute le cœur sur la cane de la gorge, et ne touche pas la gorge mais la remet selon sa figure naturelle; et puis il est avenant, et laisse quelques jours, puis il est curé d'huiles déséchans jusqu'à ce qu'il soit sain; et si la plaie a fait impression dans l'os, alors la quire; et s'il y a des pieces d'os, alors les traites tous se tu peux, et celles que tu ne peux avoir, alors laisse tant que la plaie pourrisse, et soit dégagée et alliée le issue; et si la plaie est fraîche, alors poudre sur la poudre que j'ai dit.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound caused by a lance or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then observe whether there are signs of festering beneath the wound that the patient may succumb: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, but fresh to its entire depth with blood, then do not put powder on it at first hour nor bind it for the blood that does not congeal in depth, and revive the heart, and kill the patient; but put atractif ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasms, nor bad tremors of heart constriction; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then cure the tents and other cures until they are healed; and if it cannot heal, nor work, know then that there is a fistula; so cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or slash with a sword or knife, and it's simple, or worse, on the face or back, then cure what's in front; if it's large, by stitching; if it's small, by powder; and if it's pressed into bone and has split apart, let the wound open up, and treat the pieces of flesh that are detached; and if they're not detached, then leave the wound to dry out, so that the extractions will be easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, make a judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruptions of the belly are great and medium and small; from a large wound, sometimes the intestines or the guts of the intestines will burst forth, which causes obstruction to their entrance; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes it's better for a small wound than a great one, because when you put the intestines back in, they become inflamed as soon as they feel cold, so they enter more slowly, and that makes the medium-sized wound worse; therefore it's necessary to return the intestine to its place, just like the others. And know that there are four kinds of ruptures of the belly: two common suturings occur in the belly itself, and two other proper suturings occur in other wounds of the body, and they are more proper with the suturing of the belly; I will tell each one and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	When the wound is small, and nothing is forced out of the intestines, and the wound is not grievous, it is to be treated by one of two methods: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: wet a sponge or a piece of cloth with lukewarm water only, or cook in water with squinat and cypress and spikenard, and apply the intestine until the swelling is reduced; and at times, make it redden and be careful that it does not swell.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or boil and cook malves, for through this the opening is cleared of some things; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut out hemorrhoids; and the first cure is that the wound be made smaller, so no one should cut without great necessity being present; and these are the instruments to split: so cut within the curve and do not go too far, and see where it takes shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out, set it right again according to its natural form in its proper place if you have power, for this makes moves.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the lower part under the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part under the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, make sure that the part that is injured is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to arrange what I say about great wounds and remedies.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Put the small dressings you have on hand, then take the minister with all the rupture in their hand and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of sewing, and it is that you take one or more needles according to the quantity of the wound's width, then leave a space of two fingers from the wound's head and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two skin sides with the two siphac sides, which are under the skin inside, until you make it penetrate that part, and assemble the four corners; then strain one double thread around the needle for two parts, then assemble the wound's two lips together, and leave a space of two fingers, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do so according to what you need with needles, until all the wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, for fine needles can penetrate all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot well enter: therefore it is necessary that they be moderate; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they work on the wound before the suturing; then cut the needle's ends so they do not bother the patient at night, and put tent or drapes over the needle ends to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, for it takes only one or two needles for the second sewing; it is that you assemble the two skin sides and the two siphac sides together on a needle where there is strong moderate thread; and when you have pierced these edges all four together, then remove the needle from the part where you began, in the manner they sew drapes; and leave a space of as much as a minor finger between each sewing, this is how men do it, and I sewed a wound that one man had on his belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was over a palm's width, and the intestines were two palms wide, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up until the 15th day, and I cared for him, and he became well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle; and I did not care for him with ointment, because I was in a place where we could not find any, nor any medicine; and I placed clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he became well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and put it through from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced the skin properly in one direction, then lay the chief of the suture or seam where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again on the other side of the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew just as the pelter maker sews fur, and that you leave once the suture on one side and take it up on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, who assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, and apploient l'un des chief dou syfac a l'autre chief, en tel maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, and fai percier celui leu soulement, and laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l'aguille, and la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc'a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l'un et l'autre des la partie defuers jusc'a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l'autre costeit; and c'est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens thus said this word, and any testify, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when there is an incision in the belly, then the sewing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: and is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even as the fire has changed it, so put on the intestine, and the cloth; then put powder in a jar, and if the fire has changed it, so put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and cut off the thread, and tie up the stitches, and the bandages; then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to heal, a piece of old cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in many situations where wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will not cause community with principal members, then it is necessary to put linseed oil lightly heated or rose oil around the edges, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or purulence in the bowels, and this often happens, then cleanse them with black wine vinegar, and similarly if the purulence comes just to the intestine; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the dryness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approaching nature of its parts to the natures.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the ligature jumps out of the wound, then put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned white or black, then you must tie up what is black, so that no bleeding comes from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and put the two ends hanging down on the part below the wound until the ligature falls off, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the flux of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some people, because I have seen a man wounded with a lance in the belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from there came the evacuation and the flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to subtletize until he was healed, and the edges were sewn.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it being sewn, I doubted that the patient had evil in his belly; and there was no evil, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and certain experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in this manner: take a wormwood at great horns, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the wormwood has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips so that it stretches his mouth above; and then cut the head, and it remains so that he cannot loosen it, and then put another worm after in this manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That chief if it is sewn in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine, in this manner: take the head of this thread from an intestine that is quite bare, and then tie it to the head of this thread another fine linen thread twisted, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and wind it around in folds; and this way of sewing with wormwood is not far removed from the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the innermost intestines, there is no remedy or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it swells, is universally called "fistula", and likewise when it breaks open and runs away.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the greenish-white nodation, hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it breaks open like a bird's feather; and sometimes clear fluid flows forth, and at other times thickly; sometimes little, and at other times enough; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and has no flesh is nothing but due to one of the nine causes: namely, through lack of blood or body; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much fluid; or the skin is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a sign of pestilence; or because the region's property is slow in digestion and delayed in healing, and it falls short by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and cures for medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of fistula which is done by hand work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Saiches that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for it is fistulas that come to great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so also comes to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if any fistula does not come just to what I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know how to examine it, then take a linen or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, search it out; and if the fistula is twisted, search for a subtle tent of cloth, because the cloth bends around the twisting; and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well search it with tents, then cleanse it by one of the perforations, for the moisture is short from one perforation to another, and will clean it; then bleed as much as you know, whether there be bone or nerve, and make a deep incision, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know where it is, and whether it is far from jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in some of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the bad humor and corrupted flesh that are inside; and then cure until it is sound, and if the fistula is well healed from a right place, then it is necessary to make a deep incision as much as you can, then put moist tents in medicine poultice, and pour it just up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments in healthy flesh, until it is sound; and if it is not sound by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If vein or nerves do not wound or main principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so let it rest until all corruption is removed, then cure with things that make flesh healthy until he is healed; and if he is not healed, and returns to its former state, know that you are not yet done: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep to proceed; then there's no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there's a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with forceps, do so with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, extract all of them, not leaving one; and if moisture makes it contrary, and there's no error or fear, then cut through moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound a poultice allowing corruption to spread around the bones, and let it be as long as the flesh is rotten; and then the bones will have an easier time; and if it's a large bone, such as one of the leg or hip, so reseat only the decay until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corrupted flesh and it comes close to the bone; so cover and soothe all the way up to the corruption, and then cure until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was a young man of thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body, so that the materials came out at the leg and became inflamed with a large abscess, and he had no cause to open it; but the physicians, through their foolishness, worked on it for as long as it opened up, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and there was much pus that all poured forth and moistened the body; and many physicians treated him for two years, and there was no understanding in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed out through the pus into a great mass; and the skin of the young man became red and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of those holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one of them came together with another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and dug into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and it was found to be corrupted and perforated, and the corruption extended all the way to the bone inside; I saw what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for what I removed; and began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, and could not heal; then I started again, and uncovered the bone just as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I saw it, and then removed it, and thought of sewing the place back up; but I couldn't until I dug around about a palm's length from the bone, and then pulled it all the way out to its entirety, then treated it with medicines; and it was healed and sewn quickly, and there was no need to continue the treatment except for the patient's weakness, which could not bear it, and because of my fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation it often bled, but it was made whole again, and instead of bone there grew a hard flesh, and it was in good condition and had no harm or opposition from anything at all, neither to go nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in some part of the body, then it must be done in this way: take a linen thread and strain it to the exposed end of the bone, and have someone stretch it upwards; and place another thicker linen thread on top of the flesh that is below the bone, and secure it so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath, and uncover the healthy flesh above where you see fit, so that the flesh is not injured; and put a hot iron or a wooden splint under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and it must be done as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely; then put a tisserie beneath, and then expose the corruption from one part to another, and be aware of the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and expose the bone where it contains the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other way than to cut; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or the toe of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but still it is necessary that you investigate that corrosion, how it opens up; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not work against you; and know that there are many incisors and saws for cutting these bones, according to the seat of the bones and their appearance, and their grossness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, or par cause defuer; and when you have medicine for that corruption by the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then one must cut off that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from death or the evil of the member's failure; and the sign is that the members become black, as if they had been burned by fire, and after becoming black, the corrosion spreads from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; thus hasten to cut off, and if it is due to the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion or viper and similar ones, then one must cut at the head of the joint, and not give space for it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut above the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy other than by the quantity of his virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut the whole foot; and if it goes up to the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no remedy except that the patient dies by lassitude; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is this: you bind it on top and underneath, and stretch one messenger down and another messenger up, and you desolder the flesh between the two messengers to a width of about a large span, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or sew, and put a piece of linen on each side, so that the seam does not touch the healthy part and causes another lesion and abscess to form.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, then cauterize the wound quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my presence: he had a burn that seemed like fiery ash, and that corrosion came first on his heel, until it consumed the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and long afterwards, the corrosion returned on his hand, and he came to me, and I put some counterirritants on him after the purging of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I would not, for I had hope of reverberating the matter; and I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became desperate all over, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have no other tale than this to make others do differently, when they are in need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Abscess comes in the flesh, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then rots and breaks open, and the pus leaps out, and the skin remains empty, just like vases; and the leather on top is as thin as delicate drapes, and do not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain", and are not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes right up to the bone or in front of it, then it is called "fistula"; and the leather is when you cut off that leather all around, and similarly when it is thin, just like drapes; and it is not harmed by its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you think that the skin is harmed, and the corruption is not in front, and the skin is thickened with flesh, then cure it with a clyster made thus: look if the breasts are large, and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then take Egyptian medicine made thus: take equal parts of aloe, oil, and litharge, mix them together in a vessel over fire until the medicine is red and thick like honey; then take as much as you need, and make it into a clyster with water and honey, and put it in the breast, and stop the opening; and leave the medicine there for two hours, then draw it out by squeezing; do this many times until the breasts are cleansed, and all the pus is gone; and sometimes use a clyster of ashwater when this medicine is not present, which is to take ashes from grapevine, pour water on them, let them settle, and then use as a clyster, until you know that the breasts are well cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor can the Egyptian medicine or ashwater, then use a clyster of water and honey with a little litharge mixed in; or you can use a clyster made from honey and wine, which has properties to cleanse and wash, and makes the skin healthy; and when you have done this, and think that the breasts are well cleansed, then use an ointment that brings forth flesh, which is to take diaphanite emplastrum, mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can use some medicines and ointments whose properties I have described in treating ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the clyster cannot enter it, then enlarge it slightly with a piece of iron, and apply an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then close it up and leave just enough for the clyster to enter, and if the pus that comes out has a foul odor above, then cut or lower it so that it is below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is deeply embedded, do not allow it to remain so; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see fit, arrange things in such a way that the bow runs down to the lowest point possible; for when the bow is deeply embedded, do not allow it to remain so, and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see fit, arrange things in such a way: that the bow runs smoothly downward, and does not leave anything of the bow behind; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and spread linen cloths over all the wound; then cover strongly where the perforation is larger than the first one, afterwards anoint gently with oil on another cloth according to the quantity of the perforation, and place it on the perforation of the breast to relieve the bow, and do not remove the large cloth that remains after many days once; and he who is on the perforation of the breast often removes for the purpose of removing the bow, and knows what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested or indigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in this way and you see the nature that emerges on the perforation of the breast, then know that the breasts are healed, and approaching health; and then release it in the morning, or the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts discharge undigested milk after many days, know that the breasts are not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair at all of one's health, for good health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people who take a long time to recover from their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food jumps out of the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not sound; and if the breasts are slow to heal and are far away, then add medicines with moist substance and dry virtue, as defined by ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment as defined, and mix it with rose oil, and rosewater equal in substance; then melt it and use it; and do the same thing when the ointment as defined is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on honey when it is on fire; then glue it to a cloth, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer aristologe long, and roots of celestial lilies, which is also like farina of vetches and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them, make powder, put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has reached its peak, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so treat fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the apostema of the lung
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is a swelling that grows under the nail of the hand or foot or by chance in other toes; and when it is hardened and one does not take care, then the abscess bursts forth and runs and bleeds so much that it follows the root of the nail, and by chance it may follow all the way; and comes to corrosion just to the bone, so that there is a stinking pain, and the joint of the toe is wide, and the color is flushed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the surplus flesh that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is very great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses against the flesh, begins to prick and bleed, then it is necessary that you place the caustic below the nail that pricks the flesh, and apply it above, and cut away this flesh subtly and gently, and put on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive in order to remove all; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et se li corrosion est en l'os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The knobby joints that are born in the hands of some people by chance are all cartilaginous, and sometimes there is one where there are bones, and sometimes one with a nail, and sometimes one that is born in the root of the jointure, or the birthplace is in some way the knobby joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in any notch of the arm bone do not move, and those who are born at the jointure of the arm bone, by chance move; the size of one who is cartilaginous is light, so it measures itself in its root like a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is hard to cure: it's best not to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or grows at the back notch, it is necessary that you file away the cartilage all the way to the bone, then file the bone to a suitable thickness for him, then care for it until he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the shoulders together comes by birth, or by sudden injury, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you file away the seam, so that the bone repairs itself according to its natural form; then put between two cloths or moist drapes soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wound is sealed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his shoulders with the palm, then cut away that swelling as it should be.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Wounds are great swollen abscesses full of melancholic humors that come to many members of the body; and more often occur in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to them sometimes purging with oil of cole, and then heal them with the balm of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The wound of iron is according to two manners: one is when you cut and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open up the vein and let it flow entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done according to this manner: first arise the leg with hot water very strong, until the thick blood is thinned out, then straighten the patient's leg from above the knee to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then lift it up and draw out the black blood as far as your hand will reach, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's body can withstand; and then bind it up, and command that they eat nothing except dry meat while excreting black stools; and recommence evacuation and purging when the wounds are full, and is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: raise the leg of the patient if there is much hair, then put it in water and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red and swollen; and if you don't have water, heat it over fire and then cut into the vein at the long part at the top of the knee or in the part below the ankle; then scrape the skin with a sharp tool and cut off the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it goes into the skin it looks like a white cord; then put the thread under, so that it is lifted from the skin, and then lift it to another needle, as you did first; then cut another size, or if you need more, do it; then lift it and cut at the toe of the foot; then train it and lift until the second size; then train it from size to size until it is all clean, then cut it off; and if you can't train and lift it, put a needle into every strong thread doubled, and lift it and train it, and put underneath the thread, and turn your hand this way and that until it comes out; and be careful not to cut, for if you do, one cannot train or lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient; and when you have trained it all, put a moist cloth on the wound with vinegar and olive oil rose; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Et if the vein is constricted and twisted and curled together, and it's not straight, as we have said, so you must cut it obliquely, but don't cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which you cauterize the vein is curved, and does not cut, so it opens up the vein; and it's of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cauterize the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inserted in legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or tree, and on land where there is no moisture; and it may happen to appear somewhere else than in the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from below the skin, just as serpents and worms move between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the swelling changes, and the vein begins to come out forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from about one and a half to two palms in length, and tie it, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it subsides a little bit forward, then wrap around the cloth and tie it; and if it's too long, cut off part of it and wrap up the remaining part, and don't cut off its root until it is completely gone; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess or putrefaction at the site, and a bad disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated slowly and slowly up to the end, and leave nothing inside the body; and sometimes this vein when it's treated is about five palms in length, or ten, and one man came to me, whose it was ten palms long, and when you cut it, it bursts into one or two holes, and perforates down to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the matter inside is emptied out, and then administer medicines to prevent putrefaction some day, and then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein many veins appear, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot, and there comes a lot of pus, and from which it sprouts rains; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vermin that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "beef disease", because it often attacks oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down the body, and one can feel it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it is going, and jumps forth; and it is accompanied by some humors, such as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarides in the belly; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it reaches the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this has often happened.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.
