When you see it being cured and drawn, one cannot do otherwise than when it goes: so it is necessary that you bind the above and below with a strong cord tightly, then cut above and draw away, and if the vein is far in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize with fire above until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or approaching the eye, so hold the skin tightly below it, then cut above, and draw away; and it is necessary to use the patient of bodily cleansing with soluble medicines for bad humors, and beware of putrid foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and it can move from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and then I looked afterwards, I saw it rising just like a worm on the shoulder, more quickly than anything, like fresh silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little afterwards ran all through the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it kept coming back around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very much astonished at how she was moving from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this illness behave in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had thought to do many things that would well move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want to, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought to myself that it was because the woman's body was thin, and her veins uncovered, and therefore appeared that constrained ventosity; and it did not seem according to this reason to those who are plump, and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	Et when you see to heal this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then tie above and below hastily; and then cut on top until those ventosities are constrained to return to their place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat the ventosities with that which hinders them, such as fetid pills and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kinds is that there are those with large points, small ones, hairy ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that hits a member so hits in two ways: either in the principal member, such as skull, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, warns you: so you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not warn you, nor is the arrow stuck deep, then take it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps the membrane which is above the brain, it is when there is numbness and swelling and fever and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixing up of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without sense of smell, or hearing; and perhaps the word and voice are lost; and jumps forth a moist white discharge resembling pustules, and also like a burn from fire; and if this sign warns you, then beware of the cure, and take out the arrow if it is not stuck in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it hits the heart is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow moves as the hairs do, and there is a flow of cold black blood, and a sense of chilliness and cold sweat, and syncope: know then without doubt that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not pierce the womb is when foam-free it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the covering of the chest, it is on the little ribs; and pours out great gall and great pain and breathes heavily; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and there is no hope of passing anything through the intestines, then there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the face and shoulders and throat and arms and shoulder and aid and spine of the back and fore-arm and calf and knee and legs, and similar members are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because that happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one person that an arrow hit the nose in the root of the night: I tried it, and led it out on the other side under the ear fat, and was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I led an arrow out of a game that hit the fat under the eye beneath the paper, and the arrow was bent back, and could only be pulled out by the point towards the fist, and it was a great Turkish bow, so light to hold without ears; the game was healed, and no bad accident came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian to the ears: I drew out the beard hairs, and refined them so much that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And draw out an arrow from a man's body where it was lodged in the abdomen, and thought he was dying; and then when he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and extracted it, and drew it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the arrow hit a man on his back and was stuck inside him, and the wound closed above; and the arrow remained inside him and did not change his natural disposition, nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man to whom an arrow struck his face, and the wound closed; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow wound in the man of the prince the king, who was struck in the neck and was slightly declining to the right side; and the arrow was fully embedded I was summoned to the treatment after it had been struck three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched for it with all subtlety, and did not feel it; and he felt the pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I placed on the wound a plaster attracting and digestive, because the wound did not swell; and the appearance of the arrow's point appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for many days, and the wound healed above, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied the fire cautery to the wound with corrosive medicine for several days, until it was open and I tested it; then I inserted my finger into the opening of the wound through that same medicine, until the tip of the arrow appeared clearly; and it went well beyond three months, then suddenly the wound became so foul that I had to put in forceps and pull it apart from both sides, but it would not come out; then I did not cease to probe and ingenuity with various instruments, until I got a grip on the forceps one day, made according to what its shape will become at the end of this chapter, as I handled and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the nasal cartilage could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or that I have told the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot take in all; but wise masters can well enough grasp a small thing, and on what is present and defective, find nine works, and nine instruments, at the deciphering of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from members unless they are fixed in two ways: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and that which jumps forth on the other side where it enters is an arrow entering fatty flesh, and jumping forth sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump forth now, then leave it so that the flesh is porous all around, and the exit be enlarged; and similarly if it is fixed in bone, and cannot come out, then leave it thus for some days, and move each day; and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, then drill all around with a very fine point, until the surrounding flesh is enlarged, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the skull of the head and goes just up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have described appear to the patient: then do not pull it out at all, but let it stay until it is even after some days, for if the arrow comes just so close to the spine, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck just in the bone alone, and does not come close to the spine, and the patient remains some days without bad accident, then it is fitting to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very fixed and cannot come out at all, then apply poultices around, as I have said; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body of the flesh where it cannot be seen, then it searches the whole tent; and if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut around the wound as much as possible; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it holds fast, then remove the flesh that is stuck in two parts as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you make it harder to pull out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the flesh around is softened, and then extract it, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you contrite, then administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and think how you can gently draw out the arrow without peril, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then put him according to what the sign shows.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from the other side, or if it shows something of itself, or if the skin is swollen in that place so that one can see or feel pain: then cut above, until the tongs can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for now and resume the extraction until it comes forth; and if the arrow is stuck, then apply all of its force; and if the arrow falls, and you see fit to administer poultice, then provide an instrument with a curved shape, so that the point of the arrow enters into the curvature of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is removed, then insert the instrument with its point entering inwards, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, it is necessary that you remove all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits or falls on the head, belly, bladder, or side, and it is close by, and you can reach where it hit, then remove it; and beware of cutting into the vein and nerve, then pull it out, and then cut the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium-sized, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feathers of a bird, to push forward at the point of the arrow, as follows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for cutting is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins by which one heals oneself, of which there are sixteen on the head, to wit: two batons that are after the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspirés"; and one vein that is in the forehead; and one vein that is at the chief of the nose; and the two grooves that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bleeding are two in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head" among simple people; and the median vein, which is called "fasting", is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "vein of the heart" among simple people; and the basilic vein is located on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly" among simple people; and it is above the pubic bone, and it is that which bleeds, which becomes manifestly apparent over the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the ulnar and annular bones, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the seam of the left side, and the second is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse" which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the forehead vein is as valuable as the cephalic vein for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for flux; and the quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point of it on the vein, and hold steady with your hand or other thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is clean and there is no longer a large flow.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good for the inflammation to be too severe; and the vein should not be torn in two, because the bone is close, and by chance, the inflammation may break through when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the eyelids helps those with the itch, and with the rash, and with the headache in the eye, and with face diseases; and the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it without any connection, just as before; then bleed, and let the blood flow be about a finger's length long and about a finger's width wide, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the inflammation is subtle, it may break through; then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is so valuable for ague, and for feverishness, and for diseases of the face, as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are such that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose towards his left hand, and takes a subtle flame long, and puts it inside the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start flowing now; and do not go too far in depth, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up at night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the blood.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two groins is so helpful for the constriction of the veins, and for the beginning of ulceration, and for many diseases, and for blockage, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for swelling; and the qualities of the blood are such that the patient tightens his neck below one and the other, as we said; and let the master be on top of the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a siege, then bleed the vein of the long side slightly, then draw off the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then do the same on the other side, then release the tie, and tighten the veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins above the lips so helps to clot in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and nose bleedings and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of healing are to make the patient sit before you, and hold their head as I said; then turn the book, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the small dark lines around them: cut then one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you have doubt, so cut the thicker one from each side, and similarly do to the two veins above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic healing, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the healer are to make the patient sit between your hands in the sun, and lift up the tongue, and look down on each side one black vein: heal then one and the other, and do not go too far in, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of the throat which are commonly cured are healed in two ways: or they are pricked with a sharp mint leaf, broad, or olive oil subtle like cutting instruments, and is called "anesil"; and are broad and subtle according to the breadth and narrowness of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the myrtle flame is very well known, and it is large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the thick, blood-filled veins that contain much blood and turmoil; and this is the form of olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pricked, and is for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the healer to bleed promptly and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if the artery is cut and a flow of blood comes forth, then it is necessary to stop it, as I said; and one must not prick with the knife, but cutting like anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you extract it, and change another one; or you want some remedy from it, or you let the vein flow instead of it in the arm: it opens manifestly; and cut off at the navel's edge, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the vein, then it is necessary that you extract the arm, and touch the location until you feel the pulsation; then mark the location with ink, and tie up the arm, and cut off the vein at the navel's edge; and beware that you do not strike in the artery when you see the location inflamed, for it is an artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it flow upwards just like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is arterial blood: hasten then, and place your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; tie up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be careful, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it flows, and it gushes out, and medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retreats; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Et pren une escorce de fistice, and the rend, and take one of the halves and tie it well just to the other day; if the blood does not flow, it is good; if not, then heal it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stopping is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle is so helpful that it can treat blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the squire to be aware of the nerve below, and if it points too deeply and finds the nerve, and swells and the bleeding will be grievous, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve often appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you must apply the salve to the instrument anesil; and protect the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it longwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The wound of the cephalic [head] so helps, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed at the point of the flammable olive or mint oil, for this is the most saving of all veins, because it does not have below it a nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to look for the lightest spot, and do not trouble anything if one fails the first time, and then restart; and by chance some people's joints swell up, when one fails the first time, but does not trouble anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that bleeding is not done only for the purpose of keeping healthy, but also to prevent diseases from coming; and one should bleed in one of the three veins that are said to be good: it's to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of September, and after eating, in autumn and winter, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The nurse who is entrusted with the sick has no fixed hour determined, but rather as need arises in the morning or at night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not necessary to nurse children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying only up to seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not heal the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some want to be healed, however it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse his intestines with a light enema if he has much retained wind, so that the veins do not attract superfluous substances that harm the main members; nor does one heal who is too full of meat, or drunk, until he becomes sober, or dropsy-prone; and beware of healing after a colicky passion, vomiting, bowel decorruption, frequent childbirth, vigil, watching, and multiplying; and all that can be done by virtue, whether through arms or body; then subtly balance the humors if the blood is thick, by means of foods, drinks, and medicines, if you have the power; then enter the bath, unless something hinders it, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the opening of the chest around the third hour, as we have said; and take care that day of labor, pining, and lust, and similar things; and be merry and joyful, and let the nurse be above him whom one heals, and stroke the arm two or three times, then loosen the bond moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then grease the nurse's hand with a small amount of old oil, then place her left hand on that wound below the arm where he wants to heal, so that the wound does not open and fail.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car it has veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and if there are such that are full of windiness, so that when one places a flame on them, the flame retires from the wound, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is among those; and if the vein opens, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that surgeons be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first time, it is good; if not, then one must begin again a little below or above that place in haste, unless the swelling of the limb.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is great, and the patient fears, let him wait a day or two, and do not bind the arm: by chance an abscess may form; nor enter into water, then resume the treatment if it pleases; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly, and you doubt that there will not be as much bleeding as you see, trust in this opening itself for all the flame straightly; and do some work hastily, so long as the swelling remains great; for this has often happened when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	Se you see the swelling, so do not reapply the salve and put a little bit of oil on it, because it lightens the body of blood, and is mixed with this swelling that is in the oil; and thus administer the oil to each wound that you treat veins to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing works for triplets and bowels too, when you put it on the swelling; so soften and separate the swelling when it becomes too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a big abscess comes that has happened many times, especially when it is not treated for just once or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and put a damp sponge on the swelling in water and with a little heat, and strain it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein stops, and if it remains at the swelling after some days some blackness or greenish color appears, it does not harm; and if you see, put something with aloes or myrrh soaked in calamus juice, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often it happens that an abscess and appearance arise in the healing of the wound: put then your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So take care that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance the blood flow of the artery is cut; but apply one dry poultice to harden the limb, then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become subtlety; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is weak and poor, and has need of bloodletting, that a larger wound be made to him, and the cuts be wide; and to the one who is frail, do the opposite, and he must be healed little by little, and should be healed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhaging of blood and numbness of nerve, and is more effective than the bleeding of a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in the juice of green apples; if he is overheated, bleed him three or four times; and if he has a cold complexion, moisten his bread beforehand with a sweet syrup, or with an aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he pukes blood after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he drinks a broth of pork, and a fragrant, subtle syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to swell his arm and heal it another time, so it is fitting when it is weakened by great injury, that he heals it little by little, according to the quantity of his continued vigor.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to swell his arm after the first healing, and he has strong flesh, then he heals in .vij. hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to heal on another side, then he should heal in the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body that is already heated up and brings fever; so it is necessary to drain a great quantity, and widen the wound as far as possible; then you will reward all the conditions of sickness, and put your hand on his pulse when he is recovering, so that death does not come instead of pitting, and this often happens when the nurses are neglectful; and it's not necessary when you see the arm being untied, and blood issuing a second time, and the wound is closed, to press strongly then; nor if it's curved, to stretch out the arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it alone until he recovers a second time; or you will puncture at the tip of the flame, as far as the congealed blood at the wound issues forth, and put on a poultice with oil, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then let it be and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood the second time, then let him heal in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is healed in the place of the head vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of healing is this: the patient puts his hand in hot water until the boil is red; then it is bound moderately so that the vein appears well, and then it is cut through at an angle, not straight or long; and there should be a wide hole, and the wound should be healed almost to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out without causing harm, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not reimmerse the hand in hot water, for it would be worse than in summer; and this type of wound healing is safer than all other wounds, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healing of the gallbladder wound on the right hand is worth all other diseases of the liver; and this is how to do it: strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is empty, so you can see it; and if the wound cuts across, and you cut it all around, nothing will hurt; and don't go too far inwards, for the nerves are underneath, bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is needed, then put on the vein oil and seal to solder quickly, and so do for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healing of the left hand is worth as much to the disease of mice, and do it just the same way as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wound of the sciatic nerve is worth all the diseases that are below the belly, such as diseases of the loins, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its wound are that the patient bathes their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bleeds, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and flows above the foot a great deal of pus; then it cures either a wider abscess or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are below, and the healing should be across as when sewing; and let the flames be anointed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound fails the first time, it recommences the second above a little, for the flesh is salty; nor do not doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the sciatic nerve of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its healing is worth to the pain of the groin when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his urine is such that the patient enters into a bath, and strains above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then the patient can be cleansed in all ways you can, and crossing over; and it's worth noting that you should wrap it, because the skin is sound, and she is very swollen at the hands of many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't bind it, then cleanse any rain that appears on the back of the foot and towards the little toe, and beware of nails; and do so much washing of blood as you see, and then release the bandage, and put on cotton and strain. She is now clean.
des sainies de ventouse	Of purgings by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction which is without wounding is done in two manners: either it is entirely at the surface or without being at the surface; and suction which is made by wounding and extracting blood is done on 14 parts of the body, from which some are entirely in the head; and others are in the neck; and two others in the sides of the neck; and the ventouse below the chin; and the ventouse of the shoulders; and the ventouse above the hips; and the ventouses in the arms; and the ventouses in the legs; and the ventouses in the ankles; and suction does not treat with blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it is not diminished at all, as one makes a purging of vein; and it should not be administered, neither at the surface nor without being at the surface, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the midst of the month, we will then command to lance after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose so helps the sharpness of the head giddiness that comes to the eyes, and it does not need to be done after the evacuation of all the body's waste; and this blowing is in place of the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it does not need to be used by those who are of cold complexion or have a cough, for it greatly harms them; and therefore it does not need to be used by the elderly or those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to place the poultice a little lower down due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The blowing into the neck is in place of the bleeding of the head and of the basilic vein, and therefore it is good for the constriction of the belly, and for splitting of the channel of the peritoneum, and for all, and for repletion; and it does not need to be done strongly, for if it holds too firmly, it will annoy the bladder or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, and obtalmie et emigrainne, and to the strangling, and to the pain as roots of teeth, and it is in the place of the health of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command to the patient that he extends his hand to put, that he does not cut the artery, and does not come forth with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The lancing below the chin is worth for mouth disease and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the purgings of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The lancing at the shoulders is worth for the disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, for she drains blood from these large veins; and command to the patient that he does not cut too much by deepness, for the flesh is bare of fat, and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice that is on the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases underneath, and it is necessary that the poultice be large and made of earth, so it can well draw out; and by chance, if they were subtle, they would break; and this would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The poultices of the legs clearly cure, because they draw out blood from all the body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and uterus, and restore the flowers; and they take the place of the two shins and two ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, they cause dizziness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the poultice is that you first apply it empty, and then suck it temperately, and put it on hastily, and move it equally, and do not cease from doing so, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood; then pierce, and remove the poultices, and take heed in the disposition of the body, because there are some who have tough skin, and clear pores: thus it is necessary to strike once only, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to pierce a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we only suffice once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to let out much blood, so we repeat often; and if the blood is thick, then cut deep, and the ends should be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard, and who have many pores, that you anoint the areas of the blisters with oil: if it's in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it's in winter, with hawthorn oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter oil, or balmy oil, or oil of aniseed, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being healed has a tender skin and wide pores, there is no need to apply oil, but it must be washed after the ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the person who has a lot of moisture, should rise easily with water of myrtle, or water of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excess flesh should be lifted up with old wine, or water of sycamore, or decoction of anise or camomile, or similar things; and it is not necessary to heal with a poultice before bathing or in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours; and do not sleep after the ventosation, but must take care when he needs to be ventilated and when he is ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are healing and have cholerics, and their skin is too red and inflamed; so it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in season, and similar things; and few sweets, and beef from the shoulder, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat few small birds and pigeons; and the day that he will purge himself, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some people a little or muscat before purging, or after, to comfort the main members; and be subtle with the blood, but it does not need for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are put without causing harm are those that are put on the liver, and on the kidneys, and podagra, and on the belly and the backside and the intestines and the buttocks, for these members do not suffer harm from being struck, and one only does it to attract blood from member to member, just as we put poultices on the breasts when the baby is bleeding; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put poultices on the belly and on the backside to reduce the member; and it removes pain, whenever there is congestion or stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the congestion, or moves the stone from its place; and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the kidneys when there is retained wetness, and these poultices are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes with plain water, just as in diseases of the eye, and in such a way that one fills the poultice with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered to fire is this:
