Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont,
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus put this poultice on the member: take the candle of wax or the lining, and put it in the poultice across the stick that is in the poultice, so that the clearness be at the bottom of the poultice lest it burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and have it be on the perforation that we said, so that when you want, if there is vapor, and remove the poultice; and take the lining as before, and continue often, if you need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the poultice then which is administered in illness of pleurisy, it has no stick nor perforation, and is only administered when it is full of water, and is put on the member alone; and that is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Unsers are only administered in members where you cannot put poultices because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in those denuded of flesh, such as toes or nails, and others similar; and the quality of the user is that when you find unsers that are in sweet waters without damage, take them; and put one in sweet water until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then be cured by vein and poultice, then rub the member until it becomes red, and put on the unsers; and when they will be full and will swell, if that is a place where you can put a poultice, then put it, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the limb slightly and then in water, very well, and then grasp it; and if the swelling is too great after the bath of soap, then wet a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, then place vitriol powder or gallstones on top, and similar things, until it subsides; or you may put half a handful of peeled split peas on the limb, and let them dry at the limb, so that it will subside now; and if you need more, then take other soap.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the soap doesn't want to take, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or you may insert a needle until the swelling goes down, and then put it on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see them dripping, then powder on a little bit of alum and powdered silk, or ashes, so that they will dry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear son, that the foolish doctor is falling away from this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read letters; and therefore is estranged the science in our land, because I found none good; and know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and through experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described here in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments which are presented, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say the prologue of this book, summarizing the words and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and rest upon virtue, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or piercing comes to someone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one side and the other, unless some thing hinders you, such as weakness of the body, or children, or elderly; or if the time is not very cold, or too hot; and in case of cold cholera, I mean frosty fevers, and flesh of hare and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat greasy meats, and do not fill oneself excessively with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubts about apostematic heat, or expansion of matter to a member; so the patient revives under his primary government as he has accustomed.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary for you to nourish the patient with meats that make a great healing, or if he has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and pies, and pork belly, and eel, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment brings strength and makes the breakage heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature pour la sechor des membres ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre si com os de petis enfans; mais n'a cure ramoinne sus l'os brisiet i gros tenrons qui s'aert et joint le membre ensemble tant qu'il en force si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre et pour ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes si com nos avons dit.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakages are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is one thing, and the breakage of the ribs or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breakages that occur by rotation, and others by flexion, such as the cutting of a feather to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with wound, and breakage in a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	Et à chescune manière ait son engien et son instrument propre en la restauration selonc ce que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est connu li brisure de l’os par ceu que li léus est tors et appert bien par défaire et sone au presser de la main; et quant il n’y a tortuosité ne son au touchier et li malaides ne sent mie grand dolor se n’y a point de brisure mais il puet bien avoir tortuosité ou fendure ou petite brisure.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So it is not necessary for you to move him with your hand, but set aside the remedies that come later and then restrain him subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage that occurs in a tree, and the two parts are separated, it is necessary to set them equal now, so that abscesses do not arise; and if abscesses come, then let one day pass, until the abscesses are appeased; then set it equal to what you can easily and skillfully move, and know that the restoration of this is more easy than the restorations of that which has pieces; then strain it, as is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is stretched by two parts, whether it is arm or leg, or at your hand it is small members, or to two cords, or to one cord and at your hand; and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, then reset by all means the additions in their places as you can, and guard that through your work does not come to the patient injury or pain; and join well the two bones of the os according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel with your hand if it seems to you that he is not well: so adjust him nicely, and do not strain him too much, nor press as those who bring forth by their work warm abscess and contraction to the member, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, so chastise the patient well that he does not move it, neither while watching nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and see to it that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and it must be put into a suitable condition so that he does not feel any pain; and take care that it is set right, lest tortuosities come about when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: so it is necessary to envelop them with soft and subtle linen drapes; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: so it is necessary to envelop them with a wide and strong bandage, for the broad bands encircle all the great member and bind it equally from all parts, so that there is no gap; then tie around light stays, three or four turns depending on the member, and strain your hand slightly tight on the entire bandage, then go up to the break and bind it less, so that the break will move away a bit; and gradually soften the bandage little by little, until you take hold of a great part of the healthy place; then take another bandage, and turn around again above the broken bone; then return to the lower part of the break, and bind it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first chapter above; then put linen or drapes between the bandages, until they are all equalized; then tie everything up with a belt, and then place your well-made stays on, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, then place a hot compress on it to soothe the abscess and remove the swelling; then draw it to about half of a middle-sized cane, or of beech wood from which you make clefts, or of palm leaves, and shape according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the break is a little bit bigger and wider than the others; and be as long as it needs to be for the member's smallness or largeness; then draw it onto the splints just like you did at the first joint, then tie above with a thread, just like in the first joint over the break; tighter on top, less so below; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I've seen from the works of fools who make their bandages with twisted linen strings, and that's a great error, for the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not necessary that there be less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is hurt by the edges of the stars after the stretching in their own flesh, then he puts under them poultices made of linen or ragged wool, so that he does not injure himself.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bridle, and the bowstring is broken, I will say how to treat it hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it's not necessary to stretch all the members on the first day of a broken bone.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put on splints more than after VII or V days, or more according to the severity of the aposteme happening; and here is the manner of ancient plasters for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that remains at the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of egg, and put this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring breakage in many dispositions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not either too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of poultice restoring breaks and dislocations and torsions: take aloes, ladanium, and myrrh, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mugwort, each 20 times; and mirre and aloe, each 5 times; and alechil 9 times; and make powder, and mix it with an abundance of eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this poultice, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for twisting: take mugwort and wormwood, an equal quantity; mirre and aloes, an equal quantity; acaica, six times; Armenian bolic, ten times, and grind well, and mix with water or a lot of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and disconnected bones back into their places, and to ease the pain that occurs, and to use the bone, and to break: take new linen, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore [it] fully, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly removing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig and leaves of terrestrial sycamore, and pound them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to ease the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vervain, chamomile, flowers of violets, wheat flour, each one in equal parts; and grind, and mix with wine, and apply to the member when heated, or if the member is cold, mix with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to strengthen more than the first, when abscess comes after restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, mehlieote, and sansue, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each from one part; and grind, and confection with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it except with a wax and oil ointment, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member to restore it, things that are slightly warm and dry, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is valuable for wound and pain: take mugwort and human hair or bird quill, and visnag, and equal amounts, and pound them together, and make a poultice and the bandage.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little bit afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not loosen by hand in several days. If pain comes at the joint, or prurite, with no rest or inflammation, then hasten, and loosen it, and remove the ointment now; and take a light cloth, and a damp sponge of the sea, and dip into water, and lift up the joint, until the prurite ceases, and the pain is appeased. Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or roset oil, and tie it with a bandage, as long as you are sure of hot aposteme; and soothe the inflammation of the member, and be rid of the pain, then resume subtle binding, and a little bit of ointment, and do not strain it too hard like before; and bind so finely until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling have disappeared from all of it, and you need poultice and binding again, then start again, just as you did first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Et s'il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s'aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many types of breaks are, and diverse shapes, and the causes are destined; for there are breaks that are made by percussion with a sword, and the bones are lost all the bone just up to the spongy part which is under the bone, as is done in hewing or felling; and therefore this type of break is called "hewing".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above, without piercing, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wounds from these two breakings are great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or splitting or breaking of the arm or leg bone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persevering break, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is repaired in the bone as fine as a mouse's, and it has a small fissure, and therefore this break is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by piercing with an arrow, or falling, or similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter downward, and it becomes hair-like as cooks do when they stir the cauldrons; then the arrow goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more in those who have or had moist skulls, like that of an infant; and it happens to all these types of breaks where small pieces are separated as they are; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breakings by the stripping above them, and the probing that is attempted, and by the flesh that is corrupted which is on.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and one rubs it gently above, then the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take note of the patient's accidents, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and swelling, and numbness, and fever, and the eyes to issue forth and redden, and other similar things in more than one disposition, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no unbelievable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the skin under the bone be corrupted and the accidents that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut the broken part thus: and this is to take the patient's head in your hands, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and above the wound as soft as you can, and if bleeding comes to reveal the bone or abscess appears, then provide assistance according to what is needed; and this is to fill the area with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and there is no more bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut off the narrow portion first, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put one other cutting, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have multiple cuttings of diverse sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron indeed; and work lightly, lest you wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer cuttings with tarers, not too deep lest they penetrate outside the bone of the skull, and there should be above the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each comes into its place from the edge of the bone, so that you have tarers for all tests; and this is the form of the three manners of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one tarer on the bone and turn it to your hand as much as you know the bone is pierced; then place the tarer in another part a little bit afterwards, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertubations, and make it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the joint.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary for you to take the scraper that remains from the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more tenacious and subtler than the other incisors; and if there remain none of the small bones or no scales, then gently remove them with the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another manner of work is that which the Gauls say, which is more wholesome; and it is very strong, and this is their saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears most, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place underneath the head of this lenticular incisor, which has the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is bent in two ways, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer above, so that you easily copse all around the bone, and take good care of the membrane that is below; if it is attached to the bone, so lightly remove it, for one removes it without causing any harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break of the bone does not reach to the skin, and the bone is cut so that it is only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to take away the scales with a subtle scraper which you should have in various quantities, in order to administer the most suitable thing in each place, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So that you take away first with coarse scrapers, and then with more subtle ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and breaking subtleties, it is necessary to bring about a cause according to its direction; and this is not answered by he who has set his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is open, it is necessary that you take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled linen cloth, either two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first linen cloth; and do this as gently as you can so as not to irritate the abscess; then administer something above the other layer, and do not bind it too tightly until the wound is only held together by itself; and leave it thus for a day or two until the abscess is calmed down, then release it, and administer medicines such as roots of lily, and wheat flour, and powder of incense, and aristology, and similar things; and make powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and administer medicines without biting; and watch that the wound becomes clean, lest you leave an ointment or do not assemble a bandage, for when a bandage is assembled on the skin of the brain, it will run and perish, and cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the abscess, it will necrotize above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no harm comes except through the medicine that is applied, then it has this virtue, so you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix one drachm in a rag; then apply it to the sores; and cure them by the manner of cures that are necessary, until they are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two bones above are broken, or one against another alone, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, except it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should stop your little fingernail or file from the nail, and put that breakage evenly inside your thumb's index knuckle and on the pouch side, away from the wound, until the nail grows back according to its natural shape; and do this gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone, and it cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it equal at the top of a rod about a foot long.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the breakage is of two parts, then do it again, and hurry to restore the first part as soon as you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then file at the head of the nail with cloth strips, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you probe another part on the other side, if there is a break there; and let the probes be so big that they fill the cavities of the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And certain physicians said one must grease the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that it is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with a mixture of egg white and miller's powder; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one probes the bone with goose feathers instead of cloths, and if there is a soft cloth around it, and the break holds, and the patient breathes through it; then do as you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes to the bone while you are working on it, then put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a little pot of aquilong.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the apostemes do not come forth, then apply a poultice by leaving out, of wheat flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white; then put it on gentle cauterizations, and do not bind too tightly; and if the break in the nail is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then stretch it to suitable instruments for this, then close the wound, and care for things that pertain to char and soldering, as poultices and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nail, then care for the tent, and put in a plug of cloth, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jawbone fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below, and there is no wound ahead, and the break is above only, and is not broken in two, except for small cracks inside, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right side of the jawbone, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left side of the jawbone, then insert your index finger from the right hand, and probe the break lightly, and adjust it to the other hand by degrees, and put it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split into two, then it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or are broken, then stretch them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put a cerate on the broken jawbone, and put a double cloth on it; and put a great well-made strap or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jawbone, and tie it as tight as you can, and tell the patient to rest, and feed him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure is changing, then remove it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put an ointment on it, made from flour powder with almond oil or vetch flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put a light linen cloth on it, and if the ointments are hardening, and the patient's disposition is not changing, leave it alone until he is healed; many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, then take care that no piece of bone is removed; if necessary, remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then it is widened by fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, then apply the wound, if it is wide, and put on one of those plasters that are suitable for this, in order to prevent flesh, until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks more often in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is so according to three manners: or it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a breakage with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the breakage is without wound, that you should have two ministers, one of whom holds the assistant that feels the forceps broken; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then put the breakage in your hands, so that it forms as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor wavering.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded spear of cloth or linen, and make it thick according to your need; and straighten and lift the forceps, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you put the breakage in its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps forward because it comes out too far, then it is necessary that the patient lies somewhat on his hatred, and places under the shoulder one middle pillow, and has the ministers lower the shoulder so that the bone of the forceps is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the breakage to your hands, and if you find it debris-like, then it is necessary that you cut into it; and draw out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, then cut with one of the instruments you have; but put under the forceps this instrument, in order to guard the socket.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	et semble une cuiller, and is not shaved, and be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two cheeks, just as you see, and one large, and the other narrow, just as is the outline of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, if the wound boils, and if the abscess is small, or you doubt it will boil, then dress the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if cold abscess comes, then soak one cloth in rose oil, and in vinegar, and in oil, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put plaster on the bone made from mill powder and egg yolk, and place light splints on top, and add a small spear under the armpit if needed; then take a very wide bandage three palms in width, then place double cloth over the splints and plaster; then take a fine strap three inches long and wrap it around that bandage so that the end of the bandage is hanging down; and place the strap on the shoulder, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy arm and under the sick arm; and bind each part separately; and when you see that the ligament holds the shoulder well and you clearly see that the strap does not move above the broken bone, then reward it each day; and when the ligaments relax, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder high; so that the break in the forcep will be alleviated by the adjustment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not release it unless bad accidents occur, for up to twenty days; then reapply the plaster if you see that he needs it, and strain and leave it thus until he is restored; and he is restored within twenty-eight days, or less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breakage of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder breaks or is separated from its place, and it is not known what is done except by touch; if the appearance is according to the figure of the break, and it is reset according to its natural form in all ways that you can; then put powder from the mill with an abundance of eggs, and light bandages, and put on a double cloth; then put on a large and subtle plate, a little more than the shoulder, and under the plate are threads in any place of the shoulder, so tie those threads with linen bandages so that the plate stays evenly; and then hold it tightly with a great bandage so that the plate does not move from its place, and look after it each day; and every time it swells, hold it tight, and put the plate back in its original position if it gets out of place, and have the patient sit on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25, And when this number is complete, then release it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that sets itself lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes before and points under the key, then make sure it is secured, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breakage of the forceps to calm hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breakage of the breast
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, then it falls down below, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks ease, and all, and by chance may vomit blood, and opens up the cracks in the broken bone, and thinks himself well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies somewhat on their back, and places a pillow between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of both sides to your hands, and does so in all ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then applies dressings and stoppers above the subtle steel of salt or other light material, and wraps it in a cloth, and binds it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turns the bond back around to the back, and tightens it properly, and rewards each hour the bond, and if it loosens, then tightens it again; and if it becomes necessary to release it for corrosion or itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hasten and release it, and remove the dressing, and addresses what has come to be done in ways of cures; then rewrap the dressing, and tighten it until they are well.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not occur except in large men after the back and at the top inside, and they bend only because they are flabby; and one knows this by examination of the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you set the break even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put a poultice, and strain it with an iron, if you have need of it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, just like pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and he will bleed at the points, vomit and spit up a great deal of blood, and this is grievous sickness, and the ancients have put great ingenuity.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, in order to push the break away from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless hot abscesses come there, if it is necessary.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should apply poultices on the place to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the poultice will draw away the superfluities from the place due to the weakness of the flesh.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the place with moist wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to set the flesh even around it, then be cured with the cure of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone that is pointing to the skin, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to cut on the site of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something below for fear of the sac; and then one must cut the bone, and draw it out lightly, and then sew shut the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat with poultices, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, put moist cloths on it in rose oil, and set a poultice on the place; and take care of the place as is necessary for the abscess, and be careful to watch over it on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes comes a break to the bone of the neck, and it bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if you see their hands softening and swelling and dying, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when one constrains and pricks them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient is healed, if one puts care into it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if the accidents are in the hands, and on the back there is ventosity and evacuation without will; and when one has soothed it over their belly, there is evacuation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is seized on his back and wishes to settle down, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knows it is mortal: if he does not labor at all in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the thing is more gentle.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is hot abscess, then put oil of rose or oil of egg white on the spine, until it is pacified; then put a soothing and drying ointment on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are dislocated, then it is necessary to cover with a poultice; and extract the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a seam, then cure with an ointment releasing fat, until he is healed; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the "joint of the knee", if there is one dislocated bone, take your pouch from your left hand, and place it even with your other hand at your power, then apply the ointment and steel tool on top, if you need to; then pull it out, and if there are dislocated bones, do so, extract the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the breaking of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, then there is hardly any diminution at the top; and it becomes long, and declines to the backside, and comes to the patient with pain at the place, and piercing, and swelling of what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand up to it, until you are above the breakage; and know what the breakage is and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the top, then set that breakage straight, until it is in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is of the length, or it declines inwardly, then make the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that breakage becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, then apply an ointment, and place a wooden or horn tool on top, and strain the breakage so that it does not move; and fill in the place below the ribs, until the flesh is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses come, do not touch it, until the hot abscess is pacified, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and strain it as it should be, if there is no other bad accident; and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is what is between the neck and the head of the arm, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two manners: of which one is that you take a piece of straight wood, full of medium growth, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two pieces with two straps, and bend them upwards, and lift the patient onto a seat; then throw his broken arm onto the wood, until it comes into place, and has about halfway a curvature of wood, then bend on some heavy thing or have the attendants stretch it downwards; then place the mirror alongside the breakage, so that the breakage returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one swaddles the patient on his hatereil, and binds the hand to his neck, then commands two attendants to have one hold what is above the bridle strap in their hands, and the other hold below each link, and each stretches to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then hold the strap under the breastplate, and above the breastplate, and stretch each of the attendants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breastplate is close to the shoulder of the arm, then it is necessary that you put the strap halfway under the armpit, and the other way under the breastplate; and similarly if the breastplate is towards the elbow, then you must put the strap slightly, without labor, until the breastplate is even on the arm, and on the elbow; then place the breastplate as it should be, and tighten it, lest apostemes come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do come there, then do not hold it at all for seven days, and put a soft cloth soaked in oil of roses on the bridle strap, until the abscess is appeased; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you put an ointment on the bridle strap, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and wrap a cloth around it, and hold on to the shoulder and on to the arm, so that the arm be in its natural position, without any hindrance or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use splints, and put on the bridle strap a larger and stronger splint than the others, with one or two spaces between each splint, and have each splint be so large that it passes the bridle strap three inches from each side; then hold on to the splints, in the manner I said at the beginning of this chapter on the bridle strap, more strongly and less moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.
