Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in this manner as we have said, so you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft cord on both heels and both knees, and let the sick leg be stretched two doits longer than the others; then hang it from the top of a beam, and place it on the ground two long arms away; then command one servant to embrace the chief of the buttocks, and have another servant standing with the patient, who tightly wrap the buttocks, for the joint is now returning quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at an end, then lies the patient as we have said in those with goutiness, and stretch the cord properly on the sick leg and on the hip also; then put two brands, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert the brand between the buttocks of the patient inside the form; and let there be planted moist cloths around, so that the patient does not feel pain, then each servant extend towards him, and the scribe places equal to his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If she returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place her on the table and press thus as we have said in gilbosity, and place the patient on the right side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the sick leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and put the physician's hand on the armpit of the sick hipbone, then press with the other hand, and let it stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is far away, then it's not necessary to stretch the patient down or lift them up onto the earth, but rather it should be as if one of their hanches was dislocated in the back, as we have said about lying on two hainches; and let them lie on their face, and extend the bandage as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be correct when the patient stretches out their legs, and they will be even; then bring together the thighs, and put an emplaster, and strain with a bandage, so that the hanches do not move; and if you see that they are even, then strain as before, and leave for three days or four; then release, and let it go gently, until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and backward, and behind; and does not become dislocated forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, and if she does not bend to her hip, know that he is dislocated; et li restauration de toutes si est that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and bring it between your thighs, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another servant stretches his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends well his leg to his hip slightly; and apply the poultice on, and make the leg return to the hip, and tie them together tightly for three days or four, then release him; and do not trouble the patient with walking, until the members are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, then administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of gout, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes strained and sometimes completely dislocated, inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tend towards the part where it has been dislocated: the return to its place should be gentle, and one should stretch it gently with the hands when it is only slightly displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, it is necessary that you make the patient sit upright, and hold the ministers only by the leg, above the ankle; then draw the foot to you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch upwards, and push the foot gently up; and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and drawing the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, then begin again the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a firm strap in the earth between their thighs, and tie cloths around, so as not to harm the patient; then hold the ministers by the thigh, and another minister stretches the foot to your hands or to some ligament, which is attached to the ankle of the foot; then stretch each minister equally, and the straps should be thus between the patient's thighs to retain the patient when stretching; then place the mirrors equally on the dislocation in your hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	Et quant elle iert a point, so met the plaster and bandages above, and the straps form, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the veins that are above the ankle behind, lest the bond be too tight; then leave it for 2 days or 3, and if the bond loosens, fix it; then release it on the third day or quarter, and advise the patient not to walk for 4 days; and if he walks before this term, it is not certain that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms there, you should calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, until he is healed.
des dois	you must
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the tendons are dislocated, you should have them beautifully stretched without labor, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in some notch of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a smooth or 6-inch table entirely straight, and place your foot on what appears to be these joints, then press with your foot firmly until it realigns; and when it is equal, and there is nothing amiss, then place a two-foot table under the heel of the foot, then bind with straps, and leave for 3 days, then release; and make it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: if you are not modest in your treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and unless you are pitiful and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hand if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then set the member back in place, so that the abscess cools down and becomes healthy; and when the member is in its place, then administer soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and cure the wound as it should be, with dried oils; and if with dislocation there is a break, and small bones are loosened, then remove them, and do what we have said about simple illnesses; and beware of entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will move you according to your Creator, and because of the knowledge of your arm and your body.
